No projections, no ratios, no pre-computed combinations. Let the equivariant TP layers discover which products matter. This is where unexpected physics emerges.\n22\t\n23\t### Tier 2: Engineered features (for bilinear)\n24\tProjections, ratios, nearest-ring geometry, McConnell decomposition. The bilinear model needs these because it can't construct tensor products freely.\n25\t\n26\tThe upstream model gets both tiers plus predictions.\n27\t\n28\t## Mutant Strategy (NEW - for isolation training)\n29\t\n30\t### Current: 600 more WT→ALA proteins running, capacity for 800 total\n31\t\n32\t### Three new mutant categories (~200 each):\n33\t\n34\t1. **Charge-flip (ASP→ASN, GLU→GLN)**: Changes electrostatic without changing aromatic ring. Isolates Buckingham from ring current. The delta between WT-ASP and WT-ASN is pure electrostatic correction.\n35\t\n36\t2. **Ring modification**: Changes ring electronic structure without changing backbone geometry. Options from Gemini: remove ring oxygens (TYR→PHE equivalent), remove paired ring from TRP (indole→pyrrole or indole→benzene). Tests whether the model correctly separates intensity I from geometry G in I×G.\n37\t\n38\t3. **Salt-bridge breakers (LYS→MET, ARG→LEU)**: Changes solvation environment by removing charged residues near rings. Isolates the APBS/solvation contribution. Tests whether solvated vs vacuum E-field matters.\n39\t\n40\t### Why mutants matter\n41\tEach mutant type gives the model a controlled experiment. If charge-flip mutants show the model's learned electrostatic correction matches the DFT delta, we've VALIDATED the Buckingham decomposition experimentally. That's a thesis result.\n42\t\n43\t### Tool recommendations needed\n44\t- DFT tool for running mutant calculations (ORCA r2SCAN, same as current pipeline)\n45\t- Structure preparation: need to validate mutant PDB construction (which tool? PyMOL mutagenesis? Modeller? pdb-tools?)\n46\t- Sanity checks: are the mutant structures physically reasonable before running DFT?\n47\t\n48\t## Architecture Principles\n49\t- No string-driven identity in physics code\n50\t- Protonation state is a first-class object, detected from structure, authorities consulted\n51\t- Ring type determined by the type system + protonation state, not by grepping atom names\n52\t- Every calculator's equation documented with literature reference\n53\t- One sign convention, stated once, used everywhere\n54\t- Features documented with equations, not just names\n55\t\n56\t## What went wrong with v1/v2\n57\t- v1 had the feature engineering but old physics conventions\n58\t- v2 had corrected physics but couldn't extract features\n59\t- I (Opus) kept using the v1 binary while developing v2, hiding the divergence\n60\t- Neither codebase was the truth. Both were partly wrong.\n61\t- The byte comparison exposed real v2 library bugs (histidine, graph, charges)\n62\t- The target values don't match any decomposition from the JSON -- the provenance of the old training data is unclear\n63\t- This is why a clean-room rewrite from first principles is necessary\n64\t\n65\t## Gemini's ring mutant suggestions\n66\t- Pulling oxygens off rings (TYR hydroxyl removal → effectively TYR→PHE)\n67\t- Removing second paired ring from TRP (indole → single ring)\n68\t- Worth considering alongside the three categories above\n69\t- These test ring-type-specific intensity parameters directly\n70\t"}]},"uuid":"1894fbf6-cfec-42c3-a39e-818831c18d7f","timestamp":"2026-03-31T09:12:47.640Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"dcc07331-dbb7-4ea0-aeca-1f342d76807a","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/mnt/extfast/2026thesis/biot-savart","sessionId":"08fb4581-52fd-4ae3-b548-8629b589a42d","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"temporal-launching-gizmo"}

Owns atoms, residues, conformations, and runs.\n4\t//\n5\t// A Protein has four layers:\n6\t//\n7\t//   IDENTITY (fixed):\n8\t//     Atoms:    element, name, charge — never changes\n9\t//     Residues: amino acid type, sequence position, which atoms belong\n10\t//     Topology: covalent bonds, aromatic ring membership\n11\t//\n12\t//   ENVIRONMENT (immutable after creation):\n13\t//     The physical/chemical context: BmrbEnvironment, GromacsEnvironment,\n14\t//     OrcaEnvironment, etc. Determines naming convention, force field, etc.\n15\t//\n16\t//   RUN (optional, immutable after creation):\n17\t//     Computational runs that produced conformations: GromacsRun, etc.\n18\t//     Holds per-frame metadata, FES, basins, quality metrics.\n19\t//     A conformation can optionally reference a run by index.\n20\t//\n21\t//   CONFORMATION (mutable list):\n22\t//     Where each atom IS in space. A PDB gives one. An NMR ensemble\n23\t//     gives several. An MD trajectory gives thousands.\n24\t//\n25\t//   DERIVED GEOMETRY (per conformation):\n26\t//     Ring center/normal, bond lengths/angles — computed from positions.\n27\t//     Calculated properties (APBS, ORCA, our calculators) also attach\n28\t//     to a specific conformation.\n29\t//\n30\t// Nearness:\n31\t//   Sequence nearness (residues apart) is fixed — query the Protein.\n32\t//   Distance nearness (Ångströms) varies by conformation — query it.\n33\t//   Thresholds are always parameters, never hardcoded.\n34\t//\n35\t\n36\t#include \"../Core/Types.h\"\n37\t#include \"../Atom/Atom.h\"\n38\t#include \"../Sequence/Residue.h\"\n39\t#include \"../Sequence/AminoAcid.h\"\n40\t#include \"../Sequence/ChainDescriptor.h\"\n41\t#include \"../Geometry/AromaticRing.h\"\n42\t#include \"../Geometry/CovalentBond.h\"\n43\t#include \"../Conformation/Conformation.h\"\n44\t#include \"../Run/Run.h\"\n45\t#include \"../Environment/Environment.h\"\n46\t#include <vector>\n47\t#include <memory>\n48\t#include <string>\n49\t\n50\tnamespace nmr {\n51\t\n52\t// A Protein owns everything that depends on WHAT atoms are:\n53\t//   identity (elements, names), sequence (residues), topology (rings, bonds),\n54\t//   the list of conformations, and the list of environments.\n55\t// It does NOT own per-conformation data (positions, charges, radii, E-field,\n56\t//   shielding tensors, DSSP, protonation). Those belong to Conformation.\n57\t// If it changes when the structure moves, it's on Conformation.\n58\t// If it's the same across all conformations, it's on Protein.\n59\tclass Protein {\n60\tpublic:\n61\t    // ================================================================\n62\t    // Construction\n63\t    // ================================================================\n64\t\n65\t    // Build from a PDB file. The environment specifies naming conventions.\n66\t    // If env is null, creates UnfiledEnvironment (ambiguous names fail).\n67\t    static Protein FromPdbFile(const std::string& path,\n68\t                                std::unique_ptr<Environment> env = nullptr);\n69\t\n70\t    // ================================================================\n71\t    // Atoms (fixed identities, owned)\n72\t    // ================================================================\n73\t\n74\t    size_t AtomCount() const { return atoms_.size(); }\n75\t    const Atom& AtomAt(size_t index) const {\n76\t        if (index >= atoms_.size())\n77\t            throw std::out_of_range(\"Protein::AtomAt: index \" +\n78\t                std::to_string(index) + \" >= \" + std::to_string(atoms_.size()));\n79\t        return *atoms_[index];\n80\t    }\n81\t    Atom& AtomAt(size_t index) {\n82\t        if (index >= atoms_.size())\n83\t            throw std::out_of_range(\"Protein::AtomAt: index \" +\n84\t                std::to_string(index) + \" >= \" + std::to_string(atoms_.size()));\n85\t        return *atoms_[index];\n86\t    }\n87\t\n88\t    // Add an atom. Returns its index. Takes ownership.\n89\t    size_t AddAtom(std::unique_ptr<Atom> atom);\n90\t\n91\t    // Direct access to the atom pool (for Conformation building).\n92\t    const std::vector<std::unique_ptr<Atom>>& Atoms() const { return atoms_; }\n93\t\n94\t    // ================================================================\n95\t    // Residues (fixed sequence)\n96\t    // ================================================================\n97\t\n98\t    size_t ResidueCount() const { return residues_.size(); }\n99\t    const Residue& ResidueAt(size_t index) const {\n100\t        if (index >= residues_.size())\n101\t            throw std::out_of_range(\"Protein::ResidueAt: index \" +\n102\t                std::to_string(index) + \" >= \" + std::to_string(residues_.size()));\n103\t        return residues_[index];\n104\t    }\n105\t    const std::vector<Residue>& Residues() const { return residues_; {"parentUuid":"5c8f9d35-cff7-4e9a-8474-659504ec5775","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"2369c023-2d43-4be6-b374-b4dde437adc0","agentId":"ad63c5f03d9f464ff","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_014CxUo5f5tLiqSQGmMHk1Zc","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t#pragma once\n2\t//\n3\t// Conformation: where each atom IS in a particular structural snapshot.\n4\t//\n5\t// A protein has fixed atom identities (element, name, residue membership)\n6\t// but can adopt multiple conformations: the crystal structure from X-ray,\n7\t// an NMR ensemble member, an AlphaFold prediction, an MD trajectory frame.\n8\t//\n9\t// A Conformation owns the Cartesian coordinates and lazily builds derived\n10\t// geometric structure (ring geometries, covalent bonds) that depend on\n11\t// those specific positions. Calculated properties from external programs\n12\t// (APBS electric fields, ORCA shielding tensors) also attach here because\n13\t// they are conformation-dependent.\n14\t//\n15\t// Ownership: the Protein owns Conformations. A Conformation does not\n16\t// own atoms — it references them through the Protein's atom pool.\n17\t//\n18\t\n19\t#include \"../Core/Types.h\"\n20\t#include \"../Geometry/AromaticRing.h\"\n21\t#include \"../Geometry/CovalentBond.h\"\n22\t#include \"../Protonation/ProtonationState.h\"\n23\t#include \"../Atom/Atom.h\"\n24\t#include <vector>\n25\t#include <string>\n26\t#include <map>\n27\t#include <optional>\n28\t#include <memory>\n29\t#include <stdexcept>\n30\t\n31\tnamespace nmr {\n32\t\n33\tclass Protein;  // Conformation methods may need access to the parent Protein\n34\t\n35\t// A Conformation owns everything that depends on WHERE atoms are:\n36\t//   positions, charges, radii, E-field, shielding tensors, DSSP, protonation.\n37\t// The Protein owns everything that depends on WHAT atoms are:\n38\t//   identity, sequence, topology (rings, bonds), environments.\n39\t// If it changes when the structure moves, it's on Conformation.\n40\t// If it's the same across all conformations, it's on Protein.\n41\tclass Conformation {\n42\tpublic:\n43\t    // ---- Computed state: what has been calculated for this conformation ----\n44\t    //\n45\t    // Each bit indicates that a specific calculation has been completed.\n46\t    // Accessing a property that hasn't been computed throws a clear error.\n47\t    // This prevents silent zeros from missing calculations.\n48\t    //\n49\t    enum State : uint32_t {\n50\t        HasPositions       = 1 << 0,   // AtomPositions populated\n51\t        HasCharges         = 1 << 1,   // PartialCharges loaded\n52\t        HasRingGeometry    = 1 << 2,   // Ring geometries computed\n53\t        HasBondGeometry    = 1 << 3,   // Bond geometry computed\n54\t        HasApbsField       = 1 << 4,   // APBS electric field\n55\t        HasApbsGradient    = 1 << 5,   // APBS field gradient\n56\t        HasOrcaTensors     = 1 << 6,   // ORCA DFT shielding\n57\t        HasTripeptide      = 1 << 7,   // ProCS15 tripeptide tensors\n58\t        IsProtonated       = 1 << 8,   // Protonation state assigned\n59\t        HasDssp            = 1 << 9,   // DSSP secondary structure computed\n60\t    };\n61\t    mutable uint32_t ComputedState = 0;\n62\t\n63\t    bool HasState(State s) const { return (ComputedState & s) != 0; }\n64\t    void SetState(State s) const { ComputedState |= s; }\n65\t    void RequireState(State s, const std::string& operation) const;\n66\t\n67\t    // ---- Identity ----\n68\t\n69\t    std::string Name;\n70\t\n71\t    // Provenance: \"RCSB:1UBQ\", \"OpenFold3\", \"GROMACS:md_0_100.xtc\"\n72\t    std::string Source;\n73\t\n74\t    // For trajectory frames: simulation time in picoseconds.\n75\t    // Crystal structures and predictions have TimeStampPicoseconds = 0.\n76\t    double TimeStampPicoseconds = 0.0;\n77\t\n78\t    // Which environment produced this conformation.\n79\t    // Index into Protein's Environment list. SIZE_MAX = not assigned.\n80\t    size_t WhichEnvironment = SIZE_MAX;\n81\t\n82\t    // This conformation's protonation state.\n83\t    // Starts as a copy of the environment's initial protonation.\n84\t    // Replaced if CpHMD changes it or we re-evaluate based on geometry.\n85\t    ProtonationState Protonation;\n86\t\n87\t\n88\t    // ---- Atomic positions ----\n89\t    //\n90\t    // One Vec3 per atom in the Protein, indexed identically to the\n91\t    // Protein's atom array. Position[i] is the location of Protein.AtomAt(i)\n92\t    // in this conformation.\n93\t\n94\t    std::vector<Vec3> AtomPositions;\n95\t\n96\t    // Bounds-checked position access.\n97\t    Vec3 PositionOf(size_t atomIndex) const;\n98\t\n99\t\n100\t    // ---- Derived structure (lazy, conformation-specific) ----\n101\t    //\n102\t    // Aromatic ring geometry and covalent bonds depend on atomic positions,\n103\t    // so they must be recomputed for each conformation. AromaticRing DETECTION\n104\t    // (which atoms form rings) is a sequence-level property of the Protein.\n105\t    // AromaticRing GEOMETRY (center, normal, radius) is a conformation-level property\n106\t    // computed here from these positions.\n107\t\n108\t    // ---- Per-atom conformation-dependent scalars ----\n109\t\n110\t    // Partial charges: force-field charges for THIS protonation state.\n111\t    // In CpHMD, protonation changes per frame — so charges vary per conformation.\n112\t    // For single-state work, charges are the same across all conformations.\n113\t    // Indexed by atom index i, parallel to AtomPositions.\n114\t    std::vector<double> PartialCharges;\n115\t\n116\t    // Van der Waals radii: force-field LJ σ/2 per atom (Å).\n117\t    // Used by APBS to define the molecular surface (dielectric boundary).\n118\t    // Must come from the same force field as PartialCharges —\n119\t    // mixing charge sets and radii from different force fields\n120\t    // breaks the self-consistency that makes APBS physically meaningful.\n121\t    // If empty, APBS falls back to element defaults (less accurate).\n122\t    std::vector<double> VdwRadii;\n123\t\n124\t    // ---- Derived geometry (lazy, conformation-specific) ----\n125\t    //\n126\t    // Ring GEOMETRY (center, normal, radius) depends on positions.\n127\t    // Ring TOPOLOGY (which atoms form the ring) is on the Protein.\n128\t    // Bond GEOMETRY (length, direction) depends on positions.\n129\t    // Bond TOPOLOGY (which atoms are bonded) is on the Protein.\n130\t    //\n131\t    // This structure caches geometry, not topology. The indices are\n132\t    // parallel to the Protein's AromaticRings() and CovalentBonds().\n133\t\n134\t    struct DerivedGeometry {\n135\t        std::vector<AromaticRing::Geometry> RingGeometries;\n136\t        std::vector<double> BondLengths;\n137\t        std::vector<Vec3> BondDirections;\n138\t        std::vector<Vec3> BondMidpoints;\n139\t        bool RingsComputed = false;\n140\t        bool BondGeometryComputed = false;\n141\t\n142\t        // Spatial extent of the conformation.\n143\t        Vec3 BoundingMin, BoundingMax;  // Å, axis-aligned bounding box\n144\t        Vec3 CenterOfMass;              // Å (unweighted — geometric center)\n145\t        Vec3 Extent;                    // BoundingMax - BoundingMin, per axis\n146\t        double MaxDimension;            // largest of Extent(0), (1), (2)\n147\t        double RadiusOfGyration;        // Å, sqrt(mean(|r_i - center|²))\n148\t        bool SpatialComputed = false;\n149\t    };\n150\t    mutable DerivedGeometry Derived;\n151\t\n152\t    // The SINGLE authority for ring geometry in this conformation.\n153\t    // Lazily computes and caches. }\n163\t    const std::vector<Vec3>& BondDirectionsCached() const { return Derived.BondDirections; }\n164\t    const std::vector<Vec3>& BondMidpointsCached() const { return Derived.BondMidpoints; }\n165\t\n166\t    // Spatial extent: lazily computed from AtomPositions.\n167\t    // Call EnsureSpatialGeometry() explicitly, or any accessor triggers it.\n168\t    void EnsureSpatialGeometry() const;\n169\t    Vec3 BoundingMin() const       { EnsureSpatialGeometry();  // global residue index (SIZE_MAX = none)\n181\t        double Energy = 0.0;             // DSSP energy (kcal/mol, negative = stronger)\n182\t        bool IsValid() const { return ResidueIndex != SIZE_MAX; }\n183\t    };\n184\t\n185\t    struct DsspResidue {\n186\t        char SecondaryStructure = 'C';  // H/G/I/E/B/T/S/C (Kabsch & Sander 1983)\n187\t        double Phi = 360.0;             // backbone dihedral (degrees), 360 = undefined\n188\t        double Psi = 360.0;\n189\t        double SolventAccessibility = 0.0; ============================================================================\n17\t// Biot-Savart law for a straight wire segment from a to b, at point r.\n18\t//\n19\t//   B = (mu_0 / 4pi) * I * (dl x d) / |dl x d|^2 * [angular terms]\n20\t//\n21\t// Input:  positions in Angstroms, current in nanoamperes.\n22\t// Output: B-field in Tesla.\n23\t//\n24\t// Unit conversions are explicit and use nholthaus types at the boundary.\n25\t// The inner computation uses raw doubles in SI for Eigen compatibility.\n26\t// ============================================================================\n27\t\n28\tVec3 BiotSavartRingCurrentCalculator::WireSegmentField(\n29\t        const Vec3& a_ang, const Vec3& b_ang,\n30\t        double currentNanoamperes, const Vec3& r_ang) {\n31\t\n32\t    // Explicit unit conversion at the boundary.\n33\t    // nholthaus types enforce the conversion is correct:\n34\t    //   angstrom_t → meter_t extracts the SI value.\n35\t    //   nanoampere_t → ampere_t extracts the SI value.\n36\t    // After this block, all values are in SI (metres, amperes, Tesla).\n37\t    using namespace nmr_units;\n38\t    auto toMetres = [](double angstroms) -> double {\n39\t        return Metres(Angstroms(angstroms)).value();\n40\t    };\n41\t    double I_A = Amperes(Nanoamperes(currentNanoamperes)).value();\n42\t\n43\t    Vec3 a_m = a_ang * toMetres(1.0);\n44\t    Vec3 b_m = b_ang * toMetres(1.0);\n45\t    Vec3 r_m = r_ang * toMetres(1.0);\n46\t\n47\t    // Pure SI computation from here.\n48\t    Vec3 dl_m = b_m - a_m;\n49\t    Vec3 dA_m = r_m - a_m;\n50\t    Vec3 dB_m = r_m - b_m;\n51\t\n52\t    double lenA = dA_m.norm();\n53\t    double lenB = dB_m.norm();\n54\t    if (lenA < 1e-25 || lenB < 1e-25) return Vec3::Zero();\n55\t\n56\t    Vec3 cross = dl_m.cross(dA_m);\n57\t    double crossSq = cross.squaredNorm();\n58\t    if (crossSq < 1e-70) return Vec3::Zero();\n59\t\n60\t    // B = (mu_0/4pi) * I * (dl x d) / |dl x d|^2 * (dl.dA/|dA| - dl.dB/|dB|)\n61\t    // mu_0/(4*pi) = 1e-7 T*m/A (exact in SI)\n62\t    constexpr double mu0_4pi = 1e-7;  // T*m/A\n63\t    double factor = mu0_4pi * I_A / crossSq;\n64\t    double dotTerm = dl_m.dot(dA_m) / lenA - dl_m.dot(dB_m) / lenB;\n65\t\n66\t    return factor * dotTerm * cross;  // Tesla\n67\t}\n68\t\n69\t\n70\t// ============================================================================\n71\t// Johnson-Bovey double-loop: two half-current loops at ±d from ring plane.\n72\t// ============================================================================\n73\t\n74\tVec3 BiotSavartRingCurrentCalculator::JohnsonBoveyField(\n75\t        const std::vector<Vec3>& vertices,\n76\t        const Vec3& normal,\n77\t        double lobeOffset,\n78\t        double currentNanoamperes,\n79\t        const Vec3& point) const {\n80\t\n81\t    int n = static_cast<int>(vertices.size());\n82\t    if (n < 3) return Vec3::Zero();\n83\t\n84\t    Vec3 offset = normal * lobeOffset;\n85\t    double halfI = 0.5 * currentNanoamperes;\n86\t\n87\t    Vec3 B = Vec3::Zero();\n88\t    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {\n89\t        int j = (i + 1) % n;\n90\t        B += WireSegmentField(vertices[i] + offset, vertices[j] + offset, halfI, point);\n91\t        B += WireSegmentField(vertices[i] - offset, vertices[j] - offset, halfI, point);\n92\t    }\n93\t    return B;\n94\t}\n95\t\n96\t\n97\tdouble BiotSavartRingCurrentCalculator::LobeOffsetForRing(\n98\t        const AromaticRing& ring) const {\n99\t    // Per-ring-type lobe offset from the RingType table (single authority).\n100\t    // Previously used vertex count (2 values: 5-ring vs 6-ring).\n101\t    // Now uses the actual ring type (4 distinct values: HIS 0.50, TRP5 0.52,\n102\t    // TRP9 0.60, 6-ring 0.64).\n103\t    return GetRingType(ring.TypeIndex).jbLobeOffset;\n104\t}\n105\t\n106\t\n107\tVec3 BiotSavartRingCurrentCalculator::MagneticFieldFromRing(\n108\t        const Vec3& point,\n109\t        const AromaticRing::Geometry& ringGeometry) const {\n110\t    // Fallback for direct calls without ring type info.\n111\t    // Uses vertex count as proxy (legacy behavior).\n112\t    double offset = (ringGeometry.Vertices.size() <= 5) ? config_.LobeOffset5Ring.value()\n113\t                                                         : config_.LobeOffset6Ring.value();\n114\t    return JohnsonBoveyField(ringGeometry.Vertices, ringGeometry.Normal,\n115\t                              offset, 1.0, point);\n116\t}\n117\t\n118\t\n119\tMat3 BiotSavartRingCurrentCalculator::ShieldingTensorFromRing(\n120\t        const Vec3& point,\n121\t        const AromaticRing& ring,\n122\t        const AromaticRing::Geometry& ringGeometry) const {\n123\t\n124\t    // Use per-ring-type lobe offset (from RingType table, 4 distinct values).\n125\t    Vec3 B = JohnsonBoveyField(ringGeometry.Vertices, ringGeometry.Normal,\n126\t                                LobeOffsetForRing(ring), 1.0, point);\n127\t\n128\t    // Geometric kernel: G_ab = n_b * B_a * PPM_FACTOR\n129\t    // Returns the ring current CONTRIBUTION to shielding as a raw kernel.\n130\t    // Sign convention: positive G means the ring ADDS shielding at this point,\n131\t    // matching the WT-ALA delta convention (delta > 0 when ring shields).\n132\t    //\n133\t    // Previously had sigma_ab = -n_b * B_a (NMR absolute shielding convention).\n134\t    // Changed 2026-03-28: all calculators now return unsigned geometric kernels\n135\t    // for consistency. The model learns the physical sign from the data.\n136\t    Mat3 G;\n137\t    for (int a = 0; a < 3; ++a)\n138\t        for (int b = 0; b < 3; ++b)\n139\t            G(a, b) = ringGeometry.Normal(b) * B(a) * PhysicalConstants::PpmFactor;\n140\t    return G;\n141\t}\n142\t\n143\t\n144\tVec3 BiotSavartRingCurrentCalculator::MagneticFieldAtPoint(\n145\t        const Vec3& point,\n146\t        const Protein& protein,\n147\t        const Conformation& conformation) const {\n148\t\n149\t    Vec3 total = Vec3::Zero();\n150\t    const auto& geoms = conformation.RingGeometries(protein.AromaticRings());\n151\t    OperationLog::Info(\"BiotSavart::MagneticFieldAtPoint\",\n152\t        std::to_string(geoms.size()) + \" rings\");\n153\t    for (const auto& geom : geoms)\n154\t        total += MagneticFieldFromRing(point, geom);\n155\t    OperationLog::Info(\"BiotSavart::MagneticFieldAtPoint\",\n156\t        \"|B| = \" + std::to_string(total.norm()) + \" T\");\n157\t    return total;\n158\t}\n159\t"}]},"uuid":"cccc28c5-ff5f-4c40-a102-13c78e1a981f","timestamp":"2026-03-31T09:13:06.466Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"5bf53657-d3ec-4e5a-a57b-f45f6f602e4e","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/mnt/extfast/2026thesis/biot-savart","sessionId":"08fb4581-52fd-4ae3-b548-8629b589a42d","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"temporal-launching-gizmo"}

Fixed after Gemini adversarial review.\n34\t//\n35\t// The DSSP path was added 2026-03-27: Gemini review #4 showed that the\n36\t// nearest-N/O heuristic finds random surface atoms, not actual H-bond\n37\t// partners, losing the dominant R² contribution.\n38\t//\n39\t\n40\t\n41\t// Compute dipolar + isotropic tensor from a partner position.\n42\t// d = point - partner, r = |d|.\n43\t// cosTheta = cos(D-H...A angle), or 1.0 if angle is unknown.\n44\tstatic Mat3 DipolarTensor(const Vec3& d, double r, double isoCoeff,\n45\t                          double cosTheta) {\n46\t    double r3 = r * r * r;\n47\t    double r5 = r3 * r * r;\n48\t\n49\t    Mat3 T;\n50\t    for (int a = 0; a < 3; ++a)\n51\t        for (int b = 0; b < 3; ++b)\n52\t            T(a, b) = 3.0 * d(a) * d(b) / r5\n53\t                     - (a == b ? 1.0 : 0.0) / r3;\n54\t\n55\t    // Isotropic: -C * cos²(θ_DHA) / r³\n56\t    // Negative: H-bond deshields the donor proton. In the WT-ALA convention,\n57\t    // removing the aromatic H-bond partner reduces deshielding, so the\n58\t    // ring's contribution via H-bonding is negative.\n59\t    // Changed 2026-03-28: sign {"parentUuid":"4220b7bd-3a16-4c2a-a948-1d2fc92dc2bb","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"2369c023-2d43-4be6-b374-b4dde437adc0","agentId":"ad63c5f03d9f464ff","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01HbC2jpcQuLRYCtADCYJxvb","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# Physics Decomposition: Ring Current vs Buckingham\n2\t\n3\t## The key insight\n4\t\n5\tThe DFT WT→ALA mutation delta contains multiple physics contributions:\n6\t\n7\t1. **Ring current** — through-space magnetic effect from aromatic π electrons\n8\t2. **Buckingham** — electric field effect on electron cloud polarization\n9\t3. **Bond anisotropy** — magnetic susceptibility of covalent bonds\n10\t4. **H-bond** — geometry-dependent shielding from hydrogen bonds\n11\t\n12\tThese contribute to both T0 (isotropic) and T2 (anisotropic) shielding.\n13\t\n14\t## Ring current is element-INDEPENDENT\n15\t\n16\tReference: \"Nuclear Magnetic Resonance Spectroscopy. Ring-Current Effects\n17\ton Carbon-13 Chemical Shifts\" (1974, J. Am. Chem. Soc. 96, 7542)\n18\t\n19\tThe ring current shielding at a point in space depends ONLY on the\n20\tgeometry (distance, angle to ring) and the ring current intensity.\n21\tIt does NOT depend on what nucleus is at that point. The magnetic\n22\tfield perturbation from the ring current is the same for ¹H, ¹³C,\n23\t¹⁵N, ¹⁷O, ³³S at the same position.\n24\t\n25\tPhysics: σ_ring = -I × n·B(r) where B(r) is the Biot-Savart field.\n26\tB(r) is a property of the ring geometry, not the observing nucleus.\n27\t\n28\tTherefore: ring current intensities I_JB are 7 parameters (per ring type),\n29\tNOT 35 (per ring type × element).\n30\t\n31\t## Buckingham IS element-DEPENDENT\n32\t\n33\tThe Buckingham effect σ = A·E_z + B·E_z² depends on the atomic\n34\tpolarizability and paramagnetic susceptibility, which ARE element-specific.\n35\t\n36\t### Linear coefficient A\n37\t\n38\tBuckingham (1960): A_H = -2 × 10⁻¹² esu⁻¹\n39\tCase (1995): A_H = -3.43 × 10⁻¹² esu⁻¹ (DFT-fitted)\n40\t\n41\tUnit conversion: 1 V/Å = 333,564 statV/cm\n42\tA_H = -1.14 ppm/(V/Å) in our APBS units (Case value)\n43\t\n44\tElement ratios (from chemical shift sensitivity to E-field):\n45\t  H: -1.14  (Case 1995, unit-converted)\n46\t  C: -2.28  (2× H)\n47\t  N: -3.42  (3× H)\n48\t  O: -5.70  (5× H)\n49\t  S: -9.12  (8× H)\n50\t\n51\t### Quadratic coefficient B\n52\t\n53\tBuckingham (1960): B = -10⁻¹⁸ esu⁻²\n54\tB_H = -0.111 ppm/(V/Å)² in our units\n55\t\n56\tAt E = 1 V/Å: quadratic is 10% of linear\n57\tAt E = 5 V/Å: quadratic is 49% of linear\n58\tAt E = 14 V/Å: quadratic is 136% (dominates!)\n59\t\n60\tMust include E² in the physics for atoms near charged residues.\n61\t\n62\t## Correct physics model\n63\t\n64\t```\n65\tT0_pre = Σ_t I_t × G_T0_t(JB)           ring current (element-INDEPENDENT, 7 params)\n66\t       + Σ_t J_t × G_T0_t(HM)           ring current HM (element-INDEPENDENT, 7 params)\n67\t       + A_elem × E_bond                  Buckingham linear (element-DEPENDENT, 5 params)\n68\t       + B_elem × E_bond²                 Buckingham quadratic (element-DEPENDENT, 5 params)\n69\t       + f_hbond(d)                        H-bond (TBD element dependence)\n70\t\n71\tT2_pre = Σ_t I_t × G_T2_t(JB)           ring current tensor\n72\t       + Σ_t J_t × G_T2_t(HM)\n73\t       + γ_elem × EFG_T2                  Buckingham anisotropic (element-DEPENDENT)\n74\t       + Δχ × aniso_T2                    bond anisotropy (likely element-INDEPENDENT)\n75\t       + η × hbond_T2                      H-bond tensor\n76\t```\n77\t\n78\tTotal physics params:\n79\t  Ring current: 7 I_JB + 7 I_HM = 14 (element-independent)\n80\t  Buckingham: 5 A + 5 B + 5 γ = 15 (element-dependent)\n81\t  Bond aniso: 3 Δχ = 3 (element-independent)\n82\t  H-bond: 1 f + 1 η = 2 (TBD)\n83\t  Total: ~34 params\n84\t\n85\tThis is FEWER parameters than the 95-param element-dependent model\n86\t(which put element dependence in the wrong place) and physically CORRECT.\n87\t\n88\t## Why the element-dependent model worked anyway\n89\t\n90\tThe 95-param model achieved T0=0.798, T2=0.609, scale_std=0.90 — our best\n91\tresults. Why did it work if the element-dependent ring current intensities\n92\twere wrong?\n93\t\n94\tBecause the optimizer can make any parameterization work if it has enough\n95\tdegrees of freedom. With 35 I_JB params, it could absorb both ring current\n96\tAND Buckingham effects into a single set of element×ring parameters. The\n97\teffective intensity it learned for sulfur near PHE was a combination of\n98\tthe true ring current intensity (same as H) plus the Buckingham E-field\n99\teffect scaled by sulfur's polarizability.\n100\t\n101\tThe model worked NUMERICALLY but the learned parameters don't have their\n102\tintended physical meaning. Separating ring current (element-independent)\n103\tfrom Buckingham (element-dependent) makes the physics interpretable AND\n104\tshould give similar or better results with fewer parameters.\n105\t\n106\t## Implications for the thesis\n107\t\n108\t1. The element-dependent scaling of the DFT delta near aromatic rings\n109\t   is primarily a Buckingham effect, not a ring current effect.\n110\t\n111\t2. The ring current contribution can be predicted from geometry alone,\n112\t   independent of nucleus type — confirming the classical Biot-Savart model.\n113\t\n114\t3. The Buckingham contribution requires the solvated E-field (from APBS)\n115\t   and element-dependent A/B coefficients with proper unit conversion.\n116\t\n117\t4. The quadratic B·E² term is essential for atoms near charged residues\n118\t   where the linear approximation fails by more than 100%.\n119\t\n120\t5. Proper attribution of effects (ring current vs Buckingham vs H-bond)\n121\t   is both scientifically meaningful and practically useful — the larger\n122\t   NMR model receives physically interpreted contributions, not a black\n123\t   box prediction.\n124\t"}]},"uuid":"521f76bb-139c-4921-b444-d5849aeefd70","timestamp":"2026-03-31T09:13:45.579Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"4220b7bd-3a16-4c2a-a948-1d2fc92dc2bb","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/mnt/extfast/2026thesis/biot-savart","sessionId":"08fb4581-52fd-4ae3-b548-8629b589a42d","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"temporal-launching-gizmo"}

that appear in protein NMR.\n23\tenum class Element { H, C, N, O, S, Unknown };\n24\t\n25\tinline Element ElementFromSymbol(const std::string& sym) {\n26\t    if (sym == \"H\") return Element::S;\n31\t    return Element::Unknown;\n32\t}\n33\t\n34\tinline std::string SymbolForElement(Element e) {\n35\t    switch (e) {\n36\t        case Element::H: return \"H\";\n37\t        case   }\n43\t}\n44\t\n45\tinline int AtomicNumberForElement(Element e) {\n46\t    switch (e) {\n47\t        case Element::H: return 1;\n48\t        case Element::C: return 6;\n49\t        case Element::N: decomposition of a 3x3 matrix.\n58\t//\n59\t// Any 3x3 tensor sigma decomposes uniquely into three parts:\n60\t//   T0: scalar (trace/3) -- the isotropic shielding\n61\t//   T1: pseudovector (antisymmetric part) -- 3 components\n62\t//   T2: traceless symmetric tensor -- 5 components (m = -2..+2)\n63\t//\n64\t// The T2 components use isometric normalization (real spherical It uses sqrt(3) factors\n6\t// on the T2 components (CG/component normalization), NOT the isometric\n7\t// normalization used by the v2 library. This MUST be used by the feature\n8\t// extraction engine to produce byte-identical output.\n9\t//\n10\t// The v2 library's SphericalTensor::Decompose() uses isometric normalization,\n11\t// which differs by factors of sqrt(3) and sqrt(3/2). Using the wrong one\n12\t// would silently produce different features.\n13\t//\n14\t\n15\t#include \"V1Types.h\"\n16\t#include <cmath>\n17\t#include <array>\n18\t\n19\tnamespace v1 {\n20\t\n21\tstruct SphericalDecomposition {\n22\t    double T0;\n23\t    std::array<double, 3> T1;\n24\t    std::array<double, 5> T2;\n25\t\n26\t    double T2_magnitude() const {\n27\t        double sum = 0.0;\n28\t        for (int m = 0; m < 5; ++m)\n29\t            sum += T2[m] * T2[m];\n30\t        return std::sqrt(sum);\n31\t    }\n32\t};\n33\t\n34\t// Decompose a 3x3 tensor into irreducible spherical components\n35\t// Uses CG/component normalization (sqrt(3) factors on m!=0 T2 components)\n36\tinline SphericalDecomposition decompose_tensor(const Mat3& s) {\n37\t    SphericalDecomposition sd;\n38\t\n39\t    // T0 (rank 0): isotropic = Tr(sigma)/3\n40\t    sd.T0 = s.trace() / 3.0;\n41\t\n42\t    // T1 (rank 1): antisymmetric pseudovector\n43\t    sd.T1[0] = 0.5 * (s(1,2) - s(2,1));\n44\t    sd.T1[1] = 0.5 * (s(2,0) - s(0,2));\n45\t    sd.T1[2] = 0.5 * (s(0,1) - s(1,0));\n46\t\n47\t    // T2 (rank 2): traceless symmetric part\n48\t    double Sxx = s(0,0) - sd.T0;\n49\t    double Syy = s(1,1) - sd.T0;\n50\t    double Szz = s(2,2) - sd.T0;\n51\t    double Sxy = 0.5 * (s(0,1) + s(1,0));\n52\t    double Sxz = 0.5 * (s(0,2) + s(2,0));\n53\t    double Syz = 0.5 * (s(1,2) + s(2,1));\n54\t\n55\t    // CG/component normalization — includes sqrt(3) factors\n56\t    static const double SQRT3 = std::sqrt(3.0);\n57\t    static const double SQRT3_OVER_2 = SQRT3 / 2.0;\n58\t    static const double SQRT3_OVER_SQRT2 = SQRT3 / std::sqrt(2.0);\n59\t\n60\t    sd.T2[0] = SQRT3 * Sxy; return 2;\n54\t        return 1;\n55\t    }\n56\t    if (ea == \"C\" && eb == \"O\") {\n57\t        if (length < 1.30) return 2;\n58\t        return 1;\n59\t    }\n60\t    if (ea == \"N\" && eb == \"N\") {\n61\t        if (length < 1.30) return 2;\n62\t        return 1;\n63\t    }\n64\t    // All other pairs: single bond\n65\t    return 1;\n66\t}\n67\t\n68\t} // anonymous namespace\n69\t\n70\t\n71\tvoid MolecularGraph::detect_bonds(const std::vector<AtomInfo>& atoms,\n72\t                                  const std::vector<RingInfo>& rings) {\n73\t    n_atoms_ = (int)atoms.size();\n74\t    adj_.resize(n_atoms_);\n75\t\n76\t    // Build a spatial grid for O(N) bond detection\n77\t    // For proteins (N ~ 1000-5000), brute-force O(N^2) with early cutoff is adequate\n78\t    // since the maximum bond length is ~2.2 A.\n79\t    static constexpr double MAX_CUTOFF = 2.5;  // generous upper bound\n80\t\n81\t    for (int i = 0; i < n_atoms_; ++i) {\n82\t        for (int j = i + 1; j < n_atoms_; ++j) {\n83\t            double d = (atoms[i].position - atoms[j].position).norm();\n84\t            if (d > MAX_CUTOFF) continue;\n85\t            if (d < 0.4) continue;  // too close, likely duplicate or error\n86\t\n87\t            // Compute element-specific cutoff\n88\t            double cutoff;\n89\t            if (atoms[i].element == \"H\" || atoms[j].element == \"H\") {\n90\t                cutoff = BOND_TOLERANCE_H;\n91\t            } else {\n92\t                double r_i = covalent_radius(atoms[i].element);\n93\t                double r_j = covalent_radius(atoms[j].element);\n94\t                cutoff = (r_i + r_j) * BOND_TOLERANCE;\n95\t            }\n96\t\n97\t            if (d > cutoff) continue;\n98\t\n99\t            // Connectivity constraint: same residue, or adjacent backbone\n100\t            bool same_res = (atoms[i].residue_number == atoms[j].residue_number &&\n101\t                             atoms[i].chain_id == atoms[j].chain_id);\n102\t            bool peptide_bond = false;\n103\t            if (!same_res && atoms[i].chain_id == atoms[j].chain_id) {\n104\t                // C(i)-N(i+1) peptide bond\n105\t                int dn = atoms[j].residue_number - atoms[i].residue_number;\n106\t                if (std::abs(dn) == 1) {\n107\t                    bool c_n = (atoms[i].atom_name == \"C\" && atoms[j].atom_name == \"N\") ||\n108\t                               (atoms[i].atom_name == \"N\" && atoms[j].atom_name == \"C\");\n109\t                    if (c_n) peptide_bond = true;\n110\t                }\n111\t                // Also allow S-S (disulfide) across residues\n112\t                if (atoms[i].element == \"S\" && atoms[j].element == \"S\")\n113\t                    peptide_bond = true;\n114\t            }\n115\t            if (!same_res && !peptide_bond) continue;\n116\t\n117\t            Bond bond;\n118\t            bond.atom_i    = i;\n119\t            bond.atom_j    = j;\n120\t            bond.midpoint  = 0.5 * (atoms[i].position + atoms[j].position);\n121\t            bond.length    = d;\n122\t            bond.bond_order = estimate_bond_order(atoms[i].element, atoms[j].element, d);\n123\t            bond.is_backbone = is_backbone_name(atoms[i].atom_name) &&\n124\t                               is_backbone_name(atoms[j].atom_name);\n125\t            bond.is_ring_bond = is_ring_member(atoms[i], rings) &&\n126\t                                is_ring_member(atoms[j], rings);\n127\t\n128\t            int bond_idx = (int)bonds_.size();\n129\t            bonds_.push_back(bond);\n130\t            adj_[i].push_back(bond_idx);\n131\t            adj_[j].push_back(bond_idx);\n132\t        }\n133\t    }\n134\t}\n135\t\n136\t\n137\t// ============================================================================\n138\t// Hybridization assignment\n139\t// ============================================================================\n140\t\n141\tvoid MolecularGraph::assign_hybridization(const std::vector<AtomInfo>& atoms) {\n142\t    for (int i = 0; i < n_atoms_; ++i) {\n143\t        int n_bonds = (int)adj_[i].size();\n144\t        bool has_double = false;\n145\t        bool has_triple = false;\n146\t        for (int bi : adj_[i]) {\n147\t            if (bonds_[bi].bond_order >= 2) has_double = true;\n148\t            if (bonds_[bi].bond_order >= 3) has_triple = true;\n149\t        }\n150\t"}]},"uuid":"605c0c24-53b1-454f-9e80-fa4d400ea2a2","timestamp":"2026-03-31T09:14:09.145Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"5bf34051-8180-45a9-9947-970a0a433ca1","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/mnt/extfast/2026thesis/biot-savart","sessionId":"08fb4581-52fd-4ae3-b548-8629b589a42d","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"temporal-launching-gizmo"}

Biot-Savart (from v1 model/BiotSavart.h/.cpp)\n83\t// ============================================================================\n84\t\n85\t// Wire segment field (SI units: meters, Amperes, Tesla)\n86\tinline Vec3 wire_segment_field(const Vec3& a, const Vec3& b, double I, const Vec3& r) {\n87\t    Vec3 dl = b - a;\n88\t    Vec3 d_a = r - a;\n89\t    Vec3 d_b = r - b;\n90\t    double len_d_a = d_a.norm();\n91\t    double len_d_b = d_b.norm();\n92\t    if (len_d_a < 1.0e-15 || len_d_b < 1.0e-15)\n93\t        return Vec3::Zero();\n94\t    Vec3 cross = dl.cross(d_a);\n95\t    double cross_sq = cross.squaredNorm();\n96\t    if (cross_sq < 1.0e-60)\n97\t        return Vec3::Zero();\n98\t    double factor = constants::BS_PREFACTOR * I / cross_sq *\n99\t                   (dl.dot(d_a) / len_d_a - dl.dot(d_b) / len_d_b);\n100\t    return factor * cross;\n101\t}\n102\t\n103\tinline Vec3 biot_savart_field(const std::vector<Vec3>& vertices, double I_nA, const Vec3& r) {\n104\t    int n = (int)vertices.size();\n105\t    if (n < 3) return Vec3::Zero();\n106\t    double I_A = I_nA * constants::NA_TO_A;\n107\t    Vec3 r_m = r * constants::ANG_TO_M;\n108\t    Vec3 B = Vec3::Zero();\n109\t    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {\n110\t        Vec3 a_m = vertices[i] * constants::ANG_TO_M;\n111\t        Vec3 b_m = vertices[(i + 1) % n] * constants::ANG_TO_M;\n112\t        B += wire_segment_field(a_m, b_m, I_A, r_m);\n113\t    }\n114\t    return B;\n115\t}\n116\t\n117\t// Johnson-Bovey double-loop B-field\n118\tinline Vec3 johnson_bovey_field(const std::vector<Vec3>& vertices, const Vec3& normal,\n119\t                                double d_ang, double I_nA, const Vec3& r) {\n120\t    int n = (int)vertices.size();\n121\t    if (n < 3) return Vec3::Zero();\n122\t    Vec3 offset = normal * d_ang;\n123\t    std::vector<Vec3> upper(n), lower(n);\n124\t    for (int i = 0; i < n; ++i) {\n125\t        upper[i] = vertices[i] + offset;\n126\t        lower[i] = vertices[i] - offset;\n127\t    }\n128\t    return biot_savart_field(upper, I_nA * 0.5, r) +\n129\t           biot_savart_field(lower, I_nA * 0.5, r);\n130\t}\n131\t\n132\t// Johnson-Bovey per-bond B-field\n133\tinline Vec3 johnson_bovey_bond_field(const Vec3& v_i, const Vec3& v_j, const Vec3& normal,\n134\t                                     double d_ang, double I_nA, const Vec3& r) {\n135\t    Vec3 offset = normal * d_ang;\n136\t    double I_A_half = I_nA * 0.5 * constants::NA_TO_A;\n137\t    Vec3 r_m = r * constants::ANG_TO_M;\n138\t    Vec3 B = Vec3::Zero();\n139\t    Vec3 ui = (v_i + offset) * constants::ANG_TO_M;\n140\t    Vec3 uj = (v_j + offset) * constants::ANG_TO_M;\n141\t    Vec3 li = (v_i - offset) * constants::ANG_TO_M;\n142\t    Vec3 lj = (v_j - offset) * constants::ANG_TO_M;\n143\t    B += wire_segment_field(ui, uj, I_A_half, r_m);\n144\t    B += wire_segment_field(li, lj, I_A_half, r_m);\n145\t    return B;\n146\t}\n147\t\n148\t// Geometric factor: sigma_ab = -n_b * B_a * PPM_FACTOR  (NEGATIVE sign convention)\n149\tinline Mat3 ring_geometric_factor_jb(const std::vector<Vec3>& vertices,\n150\t                                     const Vec3& ring_normal, double d_ang, const Vec3& r) {\n151\t    Vec3 B = johnson_bovey_field(vertices, ring_normal, d_ang, 1.0, r);\n152\t    Mat3 factor;\n153\t    for (int a = 0; a < 3; ++a)\n154\t        for (int b = 0; b < 3; ++b)\n155\t            factor(a, b) = -ring_normal(b) * B(a) * constants::PPM_FACTOR;\n156\t    return factor;\n157\t}\n158\t\n159\t\n160\t// ============================================================================\n161\t// Haigh-Mallion (from v1 model/HaighMallion.h/.cpp)\n162\t// ============================================================================\n163\t\n164\tstruct TriangleQuadPoint {\n165\t    double lambda[3];\n166\t    double weight;\n167\t};\n168\t\n169\tinline const std::array<TriangleQuadPoint, 7>& triangle_gauss7() {\n170\t    static const double sqrt15 = std::sqrt(15.0);\n171\t    static const double a1 = (6.0 - sqrt15) / 21.0;\n172\t    static const double a2 = (6.0 + sqrt15) / 21.0;\n173\t    static const double w0 = 9.0 / 40.0;\n174\t    static const double w1 = (155.0 - sqrt15) / 1200.0;\n175\t    static const double w2 = (155.0 + sqrt15) / 1200.0;\n176\t    static const std::array<TriangleQuadPoint, 7> pts = {{\n177\t        {{ 1.0/3.0, 1.0/3.0, 1.0/3.0 }, w0},\n178\t        {{ a1, a1, 1.0 - 2.0*a1 }, w1},\n179\t        {{ a1, 1.0 - 2.0*a1, a1 }, w1},\n180\t        {{ 1.0 - 2.0*a1, a1, a1 }, w1},\n181\t        {{ a2, a2, 1.0 - 2.0*a2 }, w2},\n182\t        {{ a2, 1.0 - 2.0*a2, a2 }, w2},\n183\t        {{ 1.0 - 2.0*a2, a2, a2 }, w2},\n184\t    }};\n185\t    return pts;\n186\t}\n187\t\n188\tinline void accumulate_tensor_triangle(\n189\t    const Vec3& v0, const Vec3& v1, const Vec3& v2,\n190\t    const Vec3& r, const std::array<TriangleQuadPoint, 7>& qpts, Mat3& G) {\n191\t    double tri_area = 0.5 * (v1 - v0).cross(v2 - v0).norm();\n192\t    if (tri_area < 1e-20) return;\n193\t    for (const auto& qp : qpts) {\n194\t        Vec3 r_s = qp.lambda[0] * v0 + qp.lambda[1] * v1 + qp.lambda[2] * v2;\n195\t        Vec3 rho = r - r_s;\n196\t        double rho_mag = rho.norm();\n197\t        if (rho_mag < constants::MIN_DISTANCE) continue;\n198\t        double rho3 = rho_mag * rho_mag * rho_mag;\n199\t        double rho5 = rho3 * rho_mag * rho_mag;\n200\t        for (int a = 0; a < 3; ++a)\n201\t            for (int b = 0; b < 3; ++b)\n202\t                G(a, b) += qp.weight * tri_area *\n203\t                           (3.0 * rho(a) * rho(b) / rho5\n204\t                            - (a == b ? 1.0 : 0.0) / rho3);\n205\t    }\n206\t}\n207\t\n208\tinline void accumulate_Bfield_triangle(\n209\t    const Vec3& v0, const Vec3& v1, const Vec3& v2,\n210\t    const Vec3& r, const Vec3& n,\n211\t    const std::array<TriangleQuadPoint, 7>& qpts, Vec3& B) {\n212\t    double tri_area = 0.5 * (v1 - v0).cross(v2 - v0).norm();\n213\t    if (tri_area < 1e-20) return;\n214\t    for (const auto& qp : qpts) {\n215\t        Vec3 r_s = qp.lambda[0] * v0 + qp.lambda[1] * v1 + qp.lambda[2] * v2;\n216\t        Vec3 rho = r_s - r;\n217\t        double rho_mag = rho.norm();\n218\t        if (rho_mag < constants::MIN_DISTANCE) continue;\n219\t        double rho3 = rho_mag * rho_mag * rho_mag;\n220\t        double rho5 = rho3 * rho_mag * rho_mag;\n221\t        double rho_dot_n = rho.dot(n);\n222\t        B += qp.weight * tri_area * (n / rho3 - 3.0 * rho_dot_n * rho / rho5);\n223\t    }\n224\t}\n225\t\n226\tinline bool needs_subdivision(const Vec3& v0, const Vec3& v1, const Vec3& v2,\n227\t                              const Vec3& r, double threshold) {\n228\t    return (r - v0).norm() < threshold\n229\t        || (r - v1).norm() < threshold\n230\t        || (r - v2).norm() < threshold;\n231\t}\n232\t\n233\tstatic constexpr double SUBDIV_THRESHOLD_L1 = 2.0;\n234\tstatic constexpr double SUBDIV_THRESHOLD_L2 = 1.0;\n235\t\n236\tinline void accumulate_adaptive(\n237\t    const Vec3& v0, const Vec3& v1, const Vec3& v2,\n238\t    const Vec3& r, const std::array<TriangleQuadPoint, 7>& qpts,\n239\t    Mat3& G, int level = 0) {\n240\t    bool subdivide = false;\n241\t    if (level == 0)\n242\t        subdivide = needs_subdivision(v0, v1, v2, r, SUBDIV_THRESHOLD_L1);\n243\t    else if (level == 1)\n244\t        subdivide = needs_subdivision(v0, v1, v2, r, SUBDIV_THRESHOLD_L2);\n245\t    if (subdivide && level < 2) {\n246\t        Vec3 m01 = 0.5 * (v0 + v1);\n247\t        Vec3 m12 = 0.5 * (v1 + v2);\n248\t        Vec3 m02 = 0.5 * (v0 + v2);\n249\t        accumulate_adaptive(v0,  m01, m02, r, qpts, G, level + 1);\n250\t        accumulate_adaptive(m01, v1,  m12, r, qpts, G, level + 1);\n251\t        accumulate_adaptive(m02, m12, v2,  r, qpts, G, level + 1);\n252\t        accumulate_adaptive(m01, m12, m02, r, qpts, G, level + 1);\n253\t    } else {\n254\t        accumulate_tensor_triangle(v0, v1, v2, r, qpts, G);\n255\t    }\n256\t}\n257\t\n258\tinline Mat3 haigh_mallion_tensor_factor(const RingInfo& ring, const Vec3& r) {\n259\t    int nv = (int)ring.vertices.size();\n260\t    if (nv < 3) return Mat3::Zero();\n261\t    const auto& qpts = triangle_gauss7();\n262\t    Mat3 G = Mat3::Zero();\n263\t    for (int i = 0; i < nv; ++i) {\n264\t        const Vec3& v0 = ring.center;\n265\t        const Vec3& v1 = ring.vertices[i];\n266\t        const Vec3& v2 = ring.vertices[(i + 1) % nv];\n267\t        accumulate_adaptive(v0, v1, v2, r, qpts, G, 0);\n268\t    }\n269\t    return G;\n270\t}\n271\t\n272\tinline Vec3 haigh_mallion_B_field(const RingInfo& ring, const Vec3& r) {\n273\t    int nv = (int)ring.vertices.size();\n274\t    if (nv < 3) return Vec3::Zero();\n275\t    const auto& qpts = triangle_gauss7();\n276\t    const Vec3& n = ring.normal;\n277\t    Vec3 B = Vec3::Zero();\n278\t    for (int i = 0; i < nv; ++i) {\n279\t        const Vec3& v0 = ring.center;\n280\t        const Vec3& v1 = ring.vertices[i];\n281\t        const Vec3& v2 = ring.vertices[(i + 1) % nv];\n282\t        if (needs_subdivision(v0, v1, v2, r, SUBDIV_THRESHOLD_L1)) {\n283\t            Vec3 m01 = 0.5 * (v0 + v1);\n284\t            Vec3 m12 = 0.5 * (v1 + v2);\n285\t            Vec3 m02 = 0.5 * (v0 + v2);\n286\t            accumulate_Bfield_triangle(v0, m01, m02, r, n, qpts, B);\n287\t            accumulate_Bfield_triangle(m01, v1, m12, r, n, qpts, B);\n288\t            accumulate_Bfield_triangle(m02, m12, v2, r, n, qpts, B);\n289\t            accumulate_Bfield_triangle(m01, m12, m02, r, n, qpts, B);\n290\t        } else {\n291\t            accumulate_Bfield_triangle(v0, v1, v2, r, n, qpts, B);\n292\t        }\n293\t    }\n294\t    return B;\n295\t}\n296\t\n297\t\n298\t// ============================================================================\n299\t// McConnell bond factor (from v1 model/PeptideAnisotropy.h)\n300\t// ============================================================================\n301\t\n302\tinline double mcconnell_bond_factor(const Vec3& bond_start, const Vec3& bond_end,\n303\t                                    const Vec3& point) {\n304\t    Vec3 bond_vec = (bond_end - bond_start).normalized();\n305\t    Vec3 midpoint = 0.5 * (bond_start + bond_end);\n306\t    Vec3 to_point = point - midpoint;\n307\t    double R = to_point.norm();\n308\t    if (R < constants::MIN_DISTANCE) return 0.0;\n309\t    double cos_theta = to_point.dot(bond_vec) / R;\n310\t    double R3 = R * R * R;\n311\t    return (3.0 * cos_theta * cos_theta - 1.0) / R3;\n312\t}\n313\t\n314\t\n315\t// ============================================================================\n316\t// Peptide bond extraction (from v1 model/PeptideAnisotropy.h)\n317\t// ============================================================================\n318\t\n319\tinline std::vector<PeptideBond> extract_peptide_bonds(const   }\n349\t    std::sort(residues.begin(), residues.end(),\n350\t              [](const auto& a, const auto& b) { return a.first < b.first; });\n351\t    std::vector<PeptideBond> bonds;\n352\t    for (size_t i = 0; i + 1 < residues.size(); ++i) {\n353\t        const auto& curr = residues[i];\n354\t        const auto& next = residues[i + 1];\n355\t        if (curr.first.first != next.first.first) continue;\n356\t        if (next.first.second != curr.first.second + 1) continue;\n357\t        if (!curr.second.has_C || !curr.second.has_O || !next.second.has_N) continue;\n358\t        PeptideBond pb.chain = curr.first.first;\n364\t        bonds.push_back(pb);\n365\t    }\n366\t    return bonds;\n367\t}\n368\t\n369\tinline std::vector<SidechainCO> extract_sidechain_co(const };\n375\t    std::vector<std::pair<std::pair<char,int>, ResAtoms>> residues;\n376\t    auto find_or_add = [&](char chain, int resnum, const std::string& resname) -> ResAtoms& {\n377\t        auto key The goal: never recompute what you already know.\n6\t\n7\tEventually these serialize to postgres (per-atom arrays as binary columns,\n8\tper-conformation scalars as regular columns) and the library reads them\n9\tback instead of recomputing. (for ML features)\n95\t\n96\t\n97\t## What DSSP Gives Us (Priority)\n98\t\n99\tDSSP is the highest-value addition we don't have. Every NMR chemical shift\n100\tprediction paper uses secondary structure as a feature. It's:\n101\t- Fast (milliseconds per structure)\n102\t- Deterministic (same structure → same assignment)\n103\t- Conformation-dependent (crystal helix may unfold in MD)\n104\t- Universally cited (Kabsch & Sander 1983, updated Joosten 2011)\n105\t\n106\tPer-residue from DSSP:\n107\t```\n108\tResNum  SS   Phi     Psi     SASA   NH-O_1   NH-O_2   O-HN_1   O-HN_2\n109\t  1     C    360.0  -51.4    115    0,0.0    0,0.0    2,-0.3   0,0.0\n110\t  2     H   -57.8  -47.0     45    0,0.0    4,-2.1   0,0.0    0,0.0\n111\t  ...\n112\t```\n113\t\n114\tSS classes: H (α-helix), B (β-bridge), E (β-strand), G (3₁₀-helix),\n115\tI (π-helix), T (H-bonded turn), S (bend), C (coil/loop).\n116\t\n117\tFor our model: SS type affects backbone chemical shifts by ~5 ppm for\n118\t¹³C and ~3 ppm for ¹⁵N. This is the single largest non-ring-current\n119\tcontribution we're currently missing.\n120\t\n121\t\n122\t## Serialization Strategy\n123\t\n124\t### Phase 1: CSV (current)\n125\tPer-protein CSV files with all features. Simple, portable, fits in memory.\n126\tGood for R analysis and initial model training.\n127\t\n128\t### Phase 2: Binary arrays\n129\tPer-atom float64 arrays in binary files (like efield_solvated.bin).\n130\tFaster I/O, smaller files. One file per property per protein.\n131\t\n132\t### Phase 3: PostgreSQL\n133\tPer-atom arrays as bytea columns in postgres. Per-conformation metadata\n134\tas regular columns. Queryable: \"give me all H atoms within 5Å of a PHE\n135\tring in proteins with pH < 4 and resolution < 2Å.\"\n136\t\n137\tSchema sketch:\n138\t```sql\n139\t-- One row per conformation\n140\tconformations (\n141\t    id serial primary key,\n142\t    protein_id text references proteins(protein_id),\n143\t    name text,\n144\t    source text,\n145\t    environment_id int references environments(id),\n146\t    n_atoms int,\n147\t    rg float,\n148\t    max_dimension float,\n149\t    -- per-atom arrays as binary (n_atoms × sizeof per element)\n150\t    positions bytea,          -- n × 3 × float64\n151\t    charges bytea,            -- n × float64\n152\t    vdw_radii bytea,          -- n × float64\n153\t    apbs_efield bytea,        -- n × 3 × float64\n154\t    apbs_efg bytea,           -- n × 9 × float64\n155\t    bs_phe_tensor bytea,      -- n × 9 × float64 (per ring type)\n156\t    ...\n157\t)\n158\t```\n159\t\n160\tThe binary arrays are opaque to postgres but queryable by our code.\n161\tMetadata (Rg, n_atoms, environment) is regular SQL for filtering.\n162\tThe actual per-atom data is read into C++/Python as numpy/Eigen arrays.\n163\t"}]},"uuid":"8d12957c-11d5-44d3-905d-9ead09412c2e","timestamp":"2026-03-31T09:14:15.471Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"b3ee5627-9e78-4d34-a29d-b727a48a2cef","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/mnt/extfast/2026thesis/biot-savart","sessionId":"08fb4581-52fd-4ae3-b548-8629b589a42d","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"temporal-launching-gizmo"}

This matches e3nn's o3.spherical_harmonics output.\n21\t//\n22\t\n23\tSphericalTensor SphericalTensor::Decompose(const Mat3& s) {\n24\t    SphericalTensor st;\n25\t\n26\t    // T0: isotropic shielding = trace / 3\n27\t    st.T0 = s.trace() / 3.0;\n28\t\n29\t    // T1: antisymmetric pseudovector via Levi-Civita mapping.\n30\t    // For antisymmetric A_ij = (s_ij - s_ji)/2, the dual vector is:\n31\t    //   v_x = A_yz, v_y = A_zx, v_z = A_xy\n32\t    st.T1[0] = 0.5 * (s(1,2) - s(2,1));\n33\t    st.T1[1] = 0.5 * (s(2,0) - s(0,2));\n34\t    st.T1[2] = 0.5 * (s(0,1) - s(1,0));\n35\t\n36\t    // Traceless symmetric part: S_ij = (s_ij + s_ji)/2 - (trace/3)*delta_ij\n37\t    double Sxx = s(0,0) - st.T0;\n38\t    double Syy = s(1,1) - st.T0;\n39\t    double Szz = s(2,2) - st.T0;\n40\t    double Sxy = 0.5 * (s(0,1) + s(1,0));\n41\t    double Sxz = 0.5 * (s(0,2) + s(2,0));\n42\t    double Syz = 0.5 * (s(1,2) + s(2,1));\n43\t\n44\t    // T2: isometric real spherical harmonic basis.\n45\t    // These coefficients ensure sum|T2_m|^2 = sum S_ij^2 (Frobenius norm preserved).\n46\t    // This is required for equivariance: rotating the tensor must not change its T2 magnitude.\n47\t    //\n48\t    // Previously used sqrt(3) factors (\"component normalization\") which were NOT isometric —\n49\t    // the T2 magnitude varied by up to 33% depending on tensor orientation.\n50\t    // Fixed 2026-03-27 after Gemini adversarial review verified the anisotropy.\n51\t    //\n52\t    // Convention: real spherical harmonics Y_2^m with normalization\n53\t    //   sum_m |T2_m|^2 = sum_ij S_ij^2  (isometric / \"norm\" normalization)\n54\t    static const double SQRT2     = std::sqrt(2.0);\n55\t    static const double SQRT3_2   = std::sqrt(3.0 / 2.0);   // sqrt(3/2) for m=0\n56\t    static const double INV_SQRT2 = 1.0 / SQRT2;             // 1/sqrt(2) for m=±2 diagonal\n57\t\n58\t    st.T2[0] = SQRT2 * Sxy;                // m = -2:  sqrt(2) * Sxy\n59\t    st.T2[1] = SQRT2 * Syz;                // m = -1:  sqrt(2) * Syz\n60\t    st.T2[2] = SQRT3_2 * Szz;              // m =  0:  sqrt(3/2) * Szz  (unchanged)\n61\t    st.T2[3] = SQRT2 * Sxz;                // m = +1:  sqrt(2) * Sxz\n62\t    st.T2[4] = INV_SQRT2 * (Sxx - Syy);    // m = +2:  (Sxx-Syy) / sqrt(2)\n63\t\n64\t    return st;\n65\t}\n66\t\n67\t\n68\tMat3 SphericalTensor::Reconstruct() const {\n69\t    // Invert the isometric normalization to recover Cartesian elements.\n70\t    static const double INV_SQRT2   = 1.0 / std::sqrt(2.0);\n71\t    static const double INV_SQRT3_2 = 1.0 / std::sqrt(3.0 / 2.0);\n72\t    static const double SQRT2       = std::sqrt(2.0);\n73\t\n74\t    double Sxy = T2[0] * INV_SQRT2;\n75\t    double Syz = T2[1] * INV_SQRT2;\n76\t    double Szz = T2[2] * INV_SQRT3_2;\n77\t    double Sxz = T2[3] * INV_SQRT2;\n78\t    double Sxx_m_Syy = T2[4] * SQRT2;\n79\t\n80\t    // Recover Sxx and Syy from Szz and (Sxx - Syy), using tracelessness:\n81\t    //   Sxx + Syy + Szz = 0\n82\t    //   Sxx - Syy = Sxx_m_Syy\n83\t    double Sxx = (-Szz + Sxx_m_Syy) / 2.0;\n84\t    double Syy = (-Szz - Sxx_m_Syy) / 2.0;\n85\t\n86\t    // Reassemble: sigma_ij = T0*delta_ij + S_ij + A_ij\n87\t    // where A_ij is reconstructed from T1 via the Levi-Civita tensor.\n88\t    Mat3 result;\n89\t    result(0,0) = Sxx + T0;\n90\t    result(1,1) = Syy + T0;\n91\t    result(2,2) = Szz + T0;\n92\t    result(0,1) = Sxy + T1[2];     // S_xy + A_xy, where A_xy = +v_z\n93\t    result(1,0) = Sxy - T1[2];     // S_xy - A_xy\n94\t    result(0,2) = Sxz - T1[1];     // S_xz + A_xz, where A_xz = -v_y\n95\t    result(2,0) = Sxz + T1[1];     // S_xz - A_xz\n96\t    result(1,2) = Syz + T1[0];     // S_yz + A_yz, where A_yz = +v_x\n97\t    result(2,1) = Syz - T1[0];     // S_yz - A_yz\n98\t    return result;\n99\t}\n100\t\n101\t\n102\tdouble SphericalTensor::T2Magnitude() const {\n103\t    double sum = 0.0;\n104\t    for (double v : T2) sum += v * v;\n105\t    return std::sqrt(sum);\n106\t}\n107\t\n108\t\n109\tdouble SphericalTensor::T2SurfaceValue(double theta, double phi) const {\n110\t    // Expand the traceless symmetric part in the real spherical harmonic basis.\n111\t    // sigma_aniso(theta, phi) = sum_{m=-2}^{+2} T2[m+2] * Y_2^m(theta, phi)\n112\t    double val = 0.0;\n113\t    for (int m = -2; m <= 2; ++m)\n114\t        val += T2[m + 2] * RealSphericalHarmonicY2m(m, theta, phi);\n115\t    return val;\n116\t}\n117\t\n118\t\n119\t// Standard fully normalised real spherical harmonics for l=2.\n120\t// These satisfy integral |Y_2^m|^2 dOmega = 1.\n121\tdouble nmr::RealSphericalHarmonicY2m(int m, double theta, double phi) {\n122\t    double ct = std::cos(theta);\n123\t    double st = std::sin(theta);\n124\t    switch (m) {\n125\t        case -2: return 0.5 * std::sqrt(15.0 / PhysicalConstants::Pi) * st*st * std::sin(2.0*phi);\n126\t        case -1: return 0.5 * std::sqrt(15.0 / PhysicalConstants::Pi) * st*ct * std::sin(phi);\n127\t        case  0: return 0.25 * std::sqrt(5.0 / PhysicalConstants::Pi) * (3.0*ct*ct - 1.0);\n128\t        case +1: return 0.5 * std::sqrt(15.0 / PhysicalConstants::Pi) * st*ct * std::cos(phi);\n129\t        case +2: return 0.5 * std::sqrt(15.0 / PhysicalConstants::Pi) * st*st * std::cos(2.0*phi);\n130\t        default: return 0.0;\n131\t    }\n132\t}\n133\t"}]},"uuid":"14098197-e84f-41a9-aded-45f16ae301f1","timestamp":"2026-03-31T09:14:21.709Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"6de164fa-2f0e-4705-a687-d2a5674cba0d","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/mnt/extfast/2026thesis/biot-savart","sessionId":"08fb4581-52fd-4ae3-b548-8629b589a42d","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"temporal-launching-gizmo"}
