Let me compile the two-pass design review.\n\n---\n\n# PASS 1: CONSTRUCTIVE DESIGN\n\n## A. Object Model\n\n### Entities and Ownership\n\n**Protein** (root owner)\n- Owns: Atom list (polymorphic, by unique_ptr), Residue list (value), AromaticRing list (topology only), CovalentBond list (topology only), ChainDescriptor list, Conformation list (value), Environment list (polymorphic), Run list (polymorphic)\n- Invariant: atom identities, sequence, ring/bond topology. These never change when the protein moves.\n\n**Atom** (owned by Protein, position-free)\n- Has: Element (enum), PdbAtomName (string)\n- Subtypes: HydrogenAtom (with ParentAtomIndex), CarbonAtom, NitrogenAtom, OxygenAtom, SulfurAtom\n- Each overrides: CovalentRadius, Electronegativity, H-bond donor/acceptor\n- Does NOT know: which residue/ring/protein it belongs to. Upward references are indices, not pointers.\n- Does NOT have: partial charges (these are conformation-dependent, live on Conformation)\n\n**Residue** (owned by Protein)\n- Has: AminoAcid enum, SequenceNumber, ChainId, AtomIndices vector, ProtonationVariantIndex (-1 or index into AminoAcidType::variants)\n- Cached backbone indices: N, CA, C, O, H, HA, CB (SIZE_MAX = absent)\n- Chi angle atom indices (up to 4, cached)\n- Delegates chemistry to AminoAcidType (static singleton table of 20+1 amino acids)\n\n**Conformation** (owned by Protein, mutable state)\n- Owns: AtomPositions (Vec3 per atom), PartialCharges, VdwRadii, ProtonationState, DsspPerResidue\n- Computed state bitfield: HasPositions, HasCharges, HasRingGeometry, HasBondGeometry, HasApbsField, HasOrcaTensors, HasDssp, etc.\n- Lazy cached: DerivedGeometry (ring geometries, bond geometries, spatial extent)\n- CalculatedProperties: APBS E-field, APBS gradient, ORCA tensors, tripeptide tensors, calculator shielding results\n- Each Conformation references an Environment by index\n\n**AromaticRing** (topology on Protein, geometry on Conformation)\n- Structural identity: AtomIndices, RingTypeIndex (enum 0-7), ParentAminoAcid, ResidueIndex, FusedPartnerIndex\n- Derived: Size(), Aromaticity(), NitrogenCount(), IsFused()\n- Physical constants: delegated to RingType table via TypeIndex\n- Geometry struct: Center, Normal, Radius, Vertices -- computed per conformation\n\n**CovalentBond** (topology on Protein, geometry on Conformation)\n- Has: AtomIndexA, AtomIndexB, BondOrder (enum), BondCategory (enum), IsRotatable\n- Geometry methods take positions as argument\n\n**ProtonationState** (on Conformation, one per conformation)\n- Has: Name, pH, ProtonationTool (enum), ToolVersion\n- Contains: vector of ResidueProtonation (per titratable residue: variant name, pKa, IsCharged)\n- Lookup by residue index\n\n**Environment** (polymorphic, owned by Protein)\n- Subtypes: BmrbEnvironment (pH, temperature, ionic strength), GromacsEnvironment (force field, water model), CrystalEnvironment, OrcaEnvironment (method, basis set, prep force field), ProteinModelEnvironment (AlphaFold/OpenFold3), UnfiledEnvironment\n- Each carries: ToolContext for atom naming, InitialProtonation\n\n### Where third-party tools inject results\n\n- **DSSP**: DsspPerResidue on Conformation (secondary structure, phi/psi, SASA, H-bond partners). Called via DsspCalculator (in External/)\n- **OpenBabel**: OpenBabelTools in External/ -- used for SMILES/InChI, connectivity checking. Results don't persist as Conformation properties.\n- **APBS**: ApbsSolver in External/ -- writes E-field (Vec3 per atom) and gradient (Mat3 per atom) onto Conformation via SetApbsElectricField/SetApbsFieldGradient\n- **PROPKA/pdb2pqr**: PropkaPredictor/Pdb2pqrRunner in External/ -- produces pKa predictions, injects ProtonationState onto Conformation\n- **tleap**: Used for charge/radius assignment, topology -- results loaded via LoadChargesFromPrmtop onto Conformation\n- **ORCA**: OrcaLoader/OrcaOutputReader in External/ -- loads shielding tensors (Mat3 per atom) onto Conformation via SetOrcaShieldingTensors\n\n### Where protonation variant lives\n\nProtonationVariantIndex on Residue is the primary storage. ProtonationState on Conformation provides the authoritative assignments for titratable residues. The v2 design intent is: Residue carries a \"detected from PDB\" variant index; ProtonationState provides the \"externally determined\" assignments; when they disagree, ProtonationState wins.\n\n## B. Calculator Architecture\n\n### Base class: ShieldingCalculator\n\nEvery calculator takes `(Vec3 point, Protein& protein, Conformation& conformation)` and returns `Mat3` (raw 3x3 tensor in Cartesian basis). The base class provides:\n\n- `ShieldingTensorAtPoint()` -- default sums per-source contributions based on IteratesOver enum\n- `SphericalTensorAtPoint()` -- decomposes the Mat3 into T0/T1/T2\n- `ScaledTensorAtPoint()` -- applies OutputScaleFactor\n- `MagneticFieldAtPoint()` -- returns Vec3 (ring current calculators)\n\nPer-source dispatchers:\n- `ShieldingTensorFromRing(point, ring, ringGeometry)` for ring-iterating calculators\n- `ShieldingTensorFromBond(point, bond, positions)` for bond-iterating calculators\n- `ShieldingTensorFromAtom(point, atomPos, charge)` for atom-iterating calculators\n- Custom: HydrogenBondDipolarCalculator overrides ShieldingTensorAtPoint directly\n\n### The 8 Calculators\n\n1. **BiotSavartRingCurrentCalculator** (Rings)\n   - Johnson-Bovey double-loop model: two current loops at +/-d from ring plane\n   - Returns geometric kernel: `G_ab = n_b * B_a * PPM_FACTOR` (rank-1 by construction)\n   - v2 sign: positive (unsigned kernel; model learns sign)\n   - v1 sign: negative (`sigma_ab = -n_b * B_a * PPM`)\n   - Biot-Savart law applied to each wire segment of the ring polygon\n   - Unit conversion: Angstroms/nanoamperes at boundary, SI internally\n   - References: Johnson & Bovey (1958), Giessner-Prettre & Pullman (1969)\n\n2. **HaighMallionSurfaceIntegralCalculator** (Rings)\n   - Dipolar kernel `[3 rho_a rho_b / rho^5 - delta_ab / rho^3]` integrated over ring surface\n   - Full rank-2 T2 anisotropy (unlike Biot-Savart which is rank-1)\n   - Triangulates from centroid, 7-point Gaussian quadrature (Stroud T2:5-1)\n   - 2-level adaptive subdivision for nearby atoms\n   - References: Haigh & Mallion (1979), AREP 1980\n\n3. **McConnellBondAnisotropyCalculator** (Bonds)\n   - Dipolar kernel from bond midpoint: `T_ab = 3 d_a d_b / r^5 - delta_ab / r^3`\n   - McConnell factor: `(3 cos^2 theta - 1) / r^3`\n   - Reference: McConnell (1957)\n\n4. **CoulombElectricFieldGradientCalculator** (Atoms)\n   - EFG: `V_ab = q_i [3 d_a d_b / r^5 - delta_ab / r^3]` -- traceless (Laplace equation)\n   - Also provides E-field: `E = sum q_i d / r^3`\n   - References: Buckingham (1960), used for Buckingham shielding effect\n\n5. **PiQuadrupoleFieldCalculator** (Rings)\n   - Quadrupole potential Hessian from ring normal\n   - 4 terms: `15 dn^2 d_a d_b / r^7 - 3 dn (n_a d_b + n_b d_a) / r^5 - 3 d_a d_b / r^5 + ...`\n   - Traceless (Laplace). Prefactor Q/(4pi eps_0) absorbed by fitting.\n   - Reference: Haigh & Mallion (1979)\n\n6. **RingSusceptibilityAnisotropyCalculator** (Rings)\n   - Point dipole from ring center: same kernel as McConnell but centered on ring\n   - McConnell factor: `(3 cos^2 theta - 1) / r^3` with ring normal as bond axis\n   - Reference: McConnell (1957) applied to ring magnetic susceptibility\n\n7. **LondonDispersionContactCalculator** (Rings)\n   - Per-vertex: isotropic `-1/r^6` + anisotropic `(3 d_a d_b / r^8 - delta_ab / r^6)`\n   - London dispersion with both T0 (van der Waals shift) and T2 (orientation-dependent)\n   - Reference: London (1937), Day & Buckingham (1964)\n\n8. **HydrogenBondDipolarCalculator** (Custom)\n   - DSSP-aware path: uses Kabsch & Sander H-bond pairs, D-H...A angle\n   - Fallback: nearest N/O neighbor search\n   - Returns dipolar kernel + isotropic: `-C cos^2(theta_DHA) / r^3`\n   - Reference: Cornilescu & Bax (1999)\n\n### Sign conventions\n\nThe v2 library uses UNSIGNED geometric kernels: all calculators return the raw kernel without a physics sign. The model learns the physical sign from data. This changed 2026-03-28 from the NMR absolute shielding convention (negative). The v1 code retains the NEGATIVE convention for byte compatibility.\n\n### Units\n\nAll outputs are in Angstrom-based geometric units (not SI). The Biot-Savart calculator converts to SI internally for the wire segment formula, then the geometric kernel construction absorbs the conversion back. The PPM_FACTOR (10^6) appears in the Biot-Savart kernel.\n\n## C. Feature Extraction\n\n### Tier 1: Raw physics (for e3nn)\n\nRaw calculator outputs in natural irrep form, per source. No projections, ratios, or pre-computed combinations. The e3nn tensor product layers discover which products matter.\n\nIrrep assignments from the v1 extractor (136 L0 + 17 L1 + 35 L2):\n\n**L=0 (scalars, 136):**\n- Per-type summed G_T0 from Biot-Savart (7 scalars)\n- Total |B| field magnitude (1)\n- Ring counts at 3/5/8/12 Angstrom shells (4)\n- Ring distances (nearest 3 + mean) (4)\n- Nearest ring cylindrical coordinates: r, rho, z, theta, 1/r^3, McConnell factor, B-field cylindrical components (12)\n- Nearest ring one-hot type + decay (8)\n- Second nearest ring: r, z, G_T0, McConnell (4)\n- Multi-ring geometry: n1.n2, |n1 x n2|, G_iso_exp_sum, G_iso_var, d2/d1 (5)\n- Bond anisotropy: CO_sum, CO_nearest, CN_sum, sidechain_CO, CN_dist (5)\n- Coulomb: |E|, E.bond, E.ring_normal, |E_backbone|/|E| (4)\n- Element one-hot: H, C, N, O, S (5)\n- Z, is_backbone, is_amide_H, is_alpha_H, is_methyl (5)\n- Structural: acceptor_dist, CO_dist, CO_McConnell, n_heavy_8A, min_ring_atom_dist, edge/center ratio, B.bond_cos, CH-pi cos, is_aromatic_res, parent_sp2 (10)\n- Residue 20-mer one-hot (20)\n- Haigh-Mallion: per-type T0 (7), nearest T0, |B_HM| (9)\n- Graph: dist_to_ring, dist_to_N, dist_to_O, eneg_sum_1/2, hybridization one-hot (3), n_pi_bonds_3, is_conjugated (10)\n- Decomposed bond aniso: backbone/sidechain/aromatic McConnell factors (3)\n- APBS: |E_apbs|, E_apbs.bond (2)\n- H-bond: dist, 1/d^3, is_donor, is_acceptor, is_backbone, count_3.5A (6)\n- Dispersion: scalar_sum, n_contacts (2)\n- Aromatic field: |E_arom|, E_arom.bond, n_sidechain (3)\n- Per-type nearest: PHE/TYR/TRP/HIS distances (4)\n- Quadrupole: scalar_sum (1)\n- Ring chi aniso: scalar_sum, nearest (2)\n\n**L=1 (vectors, 17 x 3 = 51 components):**\n- B_total (pseudovector, 1o)\n- B_near1, B_near2 (pseudovector, 1o)\n- Ring normal_1, normal_2 (pseudovector, 1o)\n- Displacement dir_1, dir_2 (polar vector, 1e)\n- Bond aniso: dir_to_nearest_CO_midpoint (1e)\n- Coulomb: E_total, E_backbone (1e)\n- Structural: dir_to_nearest_acceptor, bond_direction (1e)\n- HM: B_HM_total (1o)\n- Bond aniso decomposed: dir_nearest_midpoint (1e)\n- APBS: E_apbs (1e)\n- H-bond: best_dir (1e)\n- Aromatic field: E_arom (1e)\n\nParity: B-fields and ring normals are pseudovectors (odd parity, 1o). Displacement directions and E-fields are polar vectors (even parity, 1e). Count: 6 x 1e + 10 x 1o = 16, but the manifest says 17. Need to verify.\n\n**L=2 (traceless symmetric tensors, 35 x 5 = 175 components):**\n- Per-type G_T2 from Biot-Savart (7)\n- Nearest/second nearest ring G_T2 (2)\n- Exponential-weighted G_T2_sum (1)\n- Bond aniso: T2_CO_nearest, T2_CN_nearest (2)\n- Coulomb: T2_EFG_total, T2_EFG_backbone (2)\n- HM: per-type T2 (7), nearest T2 (1)\n- Bond aniso decomposed: T2_backbone, T2_sidechain, T2_aromatic (3)\n- APBS: T2_EE (normalized E outer product) (1)\n- H-bond: T2 dipolar (1)\n- Dispersion: T2 (1)\n- Aromatic field: T2_EFG_arom (1)\n- Per-type nearest: T2 for PHE/TYR/TRP/HIS (4)\n- Quadrupole: T2 (1)\n- Ring chi aniso: T2 (1)\nAll L=2 are even parity (2e) because they come from rank-2 dipolar/traceless symmetric kernels.\n\n### Tier 2: Engineered features (for bilinear)\n\nThe bilinear model cannot form tensor products, so it needs pre-computed scalar projections and ratios. Tier 2 includes:\n- E.bond projections (Coulomb, APBS, aromatic: E dotted with bond direction)\n- E.ring_normal projections\n- cos^2 angles (McConnell, CH-pi, B.bond)\n- Distance ratios (d2/d1, min_ring_atom/ring_center)\n- Ring frame coordinates (rho, z, theta)\n- Counts within shells\n- One-hot encodings (element, residue, hybridization, ring type)\n\n## D. New Mutant Types and Feature Sensitivity\n\n### 1. Charge-flip (ASP->ASN, GLU->GLN)\n\n**What SHOULD change:**\n- CoulombEFG: E_total, E_backbone, V_ab all change (charge distribution alters)\n- APBS E-field: completely different solvation shell\n- Coulomb scalar projections: E.bond, E.ring_normal\n- H-bond calculator: different acceptor geometry (carboxylate -> amide)\n- PartialCharges on Conformation: different charge set\n- Aromatic field features: if the charged residue was near a ring, the ring's electrostatic environment changes\n\n**What should NOT change:**\n- All ring current features (Biot-Savart, Haigh-Mallion): ring geometry unchanged\n- Ring susceptibility anisotropy: ring geometry unchanged\n- Pi quadrupole: ring geometry unchanged\n- London dispersion: ring positions unchanged\n- Bond anisotropy: backbone bonds unchanged\n- Element/identity features: target atom identity unchanged\n- Graph features: hybridization, BFS distances essentially unchanged\n- Residue encoding of the TARGET atom (only the mutated residue changes)\n\n**Validation test:** If the model correctly separates Buckingham from ring current, the WT-ASP vs WT-ASN delta should be predicted entirely from Coulomb/APBS features. Ring current features should contribute zero to the difference.\n\n### 2. Ring modification (TYR->PHE)\n\n**What SHOULD change:**\n- Ring type index: TyrPhenol -> PheBenzene (different intensity, same geometry)\n- Per-type summed G_T0/G_T2: TYR bucket loses, PHE bucket gains\n- Ring one-hot encoding changes\n- Literature/effective intensity different (TYR -11.28 vs PHE -12.00 nA/T)\n- Nearest-ring type one-hot changes\n- Aromatic field: different partial charges on sidechain (OH gone)\n- H-bond: TYR OH is both H-bond donor and acceptor; PHE has neither\n\n**What should NOT change:**\n- Ring geometry: benzene ring positions nearly identical (minus OH, vertices same for 6-ring)\n- Ring frame cylindrical coordinates (r, rho, z, theta)\n- Backbone bond anisotropy\n- Coulomb from non-ring atoms\n- Graph BFS distances\n- Element/identity of target atom\n- London dispersion: vertex positions nearly identical\n\n**Validation test:** The TYR->PHE delta should be predicted by the intensity difference between TYR and PHE ring types. If the model has correctly learned that I x G factorizes, the geometric kernel G should be the same and only I changes.\n\n### 3. Salt-bridge breakers (LYS->MET, ARG->LEU)\n\n**What SHOULD change:**\n- APBS E-field: removing a +1 charge dramatically changes solvation\n- Coulomb E-field: lose long-range charge effect\n- H-bond: LYS NZ is a strong donor; MET SD is an acceptor\n- Aromatic field: if the charged residue was near a ring, electrostatic context changes\n- ProtonationState: may affect nearby titratable residues (pKa shifts)\n\n**What should NOT change:**\n- Ring current features: ring geometry unchanged\n- Bond anisotropy: backbone bonds unchanged\n- Dispersion: ring vertex positions unchanged\n- Element/identity features\n- Graph features (topology changes but BFS distances similar)\n- Quadrupole: ring geometry unchanged\n\n**Validation test:** The salt-bridge-breaker delta isolates the solvation/electrostatic contribution. If WT-LYS vs WT-MET shows a large delta for atoms near the mutation site, that delta should be captured entirely by APBS/Coulomb features, not ring current.\n\n## E. What Should NOT Be Reimplemented\n\n### Use third-party tools as authorities:\n\n1. **DSSP** (secondary structure, H-bonds, phi/psi, SASA): Kabsch & Sander (1983) is the standard. Do not reimplement H-bond detection -- DSSP's energy criterion is the accepted definition.\n\n2. **APBS** (Poisson-Boltzmann electrostatics): Solving the PBE is a multi-person-year effort. Use APBS via its C API or as subprocess. The solvated E-field and EFG are the APBS answers.\n\n3. **PROPKA/pdb2pqr** (pKa prediction, protonation assignment): pKa prediction is its own field. Accept PROPKA's assignments.\n\n4. **tleap/AmberTools** (force field charges, topology): ff14SB charges are parameterized against thermodynamic data. Do not fit our own charges.\n\n5. **ORCA** (DFT shielding tensors): Quantum chemistry is the ground truth for our targets. Run ORCA externally.\n\n6. **OpenBabel** (SMILES, InChI, connectivity): Cheminformatics data. Use as authority.\n\n### Physics we should NOT compute ourselves:\n\n- Solvation free energies\n- pKa from structure\n- Force field parameterization\n- Quantum mechanical shielding (the DFT calculation itself)\n- Hydrogen placement (use reduce or tleap)\n\n---\n\n# PASS 2: ADVERSARIAL REVIEW\n\nNow I assume Pass 1 is full of problems. Let me walk the code again looking for what I got wrong or missed.\n\n## 1. The sign convention is a time bomb\n\nThe v2 library changed to unsigned geometric kernels on 2026-03-28 (positive G in BiotSavart, line 139: `G(a,b) = ringGeometry.Normal(b) * B(a) * PPM_FACTOR`). The v1 code uses NEGATIVE: `factor(a,b) = -ring_normal(b) * B(a) * PPM_FACTOR` (V1Physics.h line 155).\n\nBut the ported EquivariantExtractor.cpp at `src/Features/EquivariantExtractor.cpp` lives in the v1 namespace and calls `ring_geometric_factor_jb()` from V1Physics.h -- which uses the NEGATIVE sign. Meanwhile, the v2 Calculator classes use the POSITIVE sign.\n\n**The problem**: if the rewrite tries to unify these into a single feature extraction pipeline that calls both v2 calculators and v1 feature engineering, the signs will be inconsistent. The bilinear model was trained on v1 features (negative convention). Switching to v2 conventions would flip the sign of every ring current feature, invalidating all trained models.\n\n**The deeper problem**: \"the model learns the sign from data\" is a convenient fiction. The model was trained on data where positive T0 means shielding and negative means deshielding. The sign convention of the geometric kernel determines whether the fitted intensity parameter is positive or negative. Changing the kernel sign and claiming \"the model handles it\" means the learned intensities flip sign -- they are no longer comparable to literature values. For the thesis, the student needs to report intensities in the same convention as Giessner-Prettre (1969). This requires explicitly choosing and documenting the NMR convention (sigma > 0 = shielding, ring current above ring = shielding, approach from above = positive z).\n\n**Recommendation**: The rewrite must commit to ONE sign convention, document it with a worked example (e.g., \"a proton 3 Angstroms above a PHE ring on the normal axis has sigma = +X ppm\"), and ensure every calculator, feature extractor, and model uses it.\n\n## 2. The T2 normalization mismatch is still lurking\n\nThe v2 library uses isometric normalization (Types.cpp lines 58-62): `T2[0] = sqrt(2) * Sxy`. The v1 code uses CG/component normalization (V1SphericalTensor.h lines 56-64): `T2[0] = sqrt(3) * Sxy`. These differ by a factor of `sqrt(3)/sqrt(2) = sqrt(3/2) ~ 1.225`.\n\nUNIFICATION_BUGS.md Bug #4 says this was fixed by \"re-decomposing using v1::decompose_tensor\". But in the rewrite, which normalization wins? The e3nn framework uses the e3nn CG convention, which is neither of these -- e3nn uses `o3.spherical_harmonics()` with `normalize=True`, producing yet another set of factors.\n\n**The problem**: there are now THREE normalizations in play. The trained bilinear model expects v1 CG normalization. The e3nn model expects e3nn's convention. The v2 library uses isometric. A \"last rewrite\" that picks one will break compatibility with at least one model.\n\n**Recommendation**: The rewrite must:\n- State which normalization is the canonical internal representation\n- Provide explicit conversion functions between all three\n- Apply the conversion at the boundary (when writing features for each model)\n- Test with a known tensor (e.g., sigma_zz = 1, all else 0) that the round-trip through decompose -> T2 components -> reconstruct gives the original matrix\n\n## 3. The Haigh-Mallion dipolar kernel is missing its prefactor\n\nThe HaighMallion calculator computes the raw dipolar kernel `3 rho_a rho_b / rho^5 - delta_ab / rho^3` and returns it directly. This is the geometry of the dipolar interaction, but it is NOT the shielding tensor. The actual Haigh-Mallion shielding involves:\n\n`sigma_ab = -(1/2c^2) * I * integral_S [3 rho_a rho_b / rho^5 - delta_ab / rho^3] dS`\n\nwhere c is the speed of light and I is the ring current. The `1/(2c^2)` prefactor and the intensity I are absent. Pass 1 said \"prefactor absorbed by fitting\" -- but this is only valid if the feature extractor knows this. If the Haigh-Mallion features are compared directly with Biot-Savart features (which include `mu_0/(4pi)` and PPM_FACTOR), their magnitudes are not on the same scale. The bilinear model can handle this with different learned coefficients per feature, but the e3nn model, which sums across all ring current contributions, will weight them incorrectly.\n\n**Recommendation**: Each calculator's output should document what physical prefactors are included vs absorbed. A \"prefactor budget\" table in the code. For the rewrite, either include all prefactors consistently or normalize all geometric kernels to the same scale.\n\n## 4. The MolecularGraph bond detection differs between v1 and the rewrite\n\nUNIFICATION_BUGS.md Bug #2 documents graph_dist_ring differing by up to 111. The root cause is bond detection: v1 uses `BOND_TOLERANCE = 1.15` (multiplicative on sum of covalent radii) and `BOND_TOLERANCE_H = 1.30` (absolute cutoff for X-H bonds). The v2 Protein::DetectCovalentBonds uses a single additive tolerance (`toleranceAngstroms = 0.4`).\n\nThese are fundamentally different criteria:\n- v1: `d < (r_i + r_j) * 1.15` -- scales with atom size\n- v2: `d < (r_i + r_j) + 0.4` -- constant offset regardless of atom size\n\nFor C-C bonds (r_i + r_j = 1.52): v1 cutoff = 1.75, v2 cutoff = 1.92. For C-H bonds (r_i + r_j = 1.07): v1 cutoff = 1.30 (absolute), v2 cutoff = 1.47. The v2 criterion detects more bonds, especially false C-H bonds. This propagates into BFS distances, hybridization, and all graph features.\n\n**Recommendation**: The rewrite should use the v1 bond detection criterion (multiplicative tolerance + absolute H cutoff). Document the choice. Add a unit test with a known protein where every bond is verified against a reference (e.g., PDB CONECT records or OpenBabel output).\n\n## 5. The HydrogenBondDipolarCalculator's fallback is scientifically wrong\n\nThe fallback path (no DSSP) finds the nearest N/O atom and computes a dipolar tensor to it. This is not an H-bond calculation -- it is a nearest-atom search. Gemini's review (#4, noted in the code comments) already identified that this finds random surface atoms, not H-bond partners. The DSSP path is correct, but if DSSP is not computed, the fallback silently produces garbage features.\n\n**The problem**: In a \"last rewrite\", there should be no fallback to wrong physics. If DSSP is required for H-bond features, then DSSP must be a prerequisite. If DSSP is unavailable, H-bond features should be zeros (explicitly missing), not wrong values that the model treats as real.\n\n**Recommendation**: Remove the fallback. Make DSSP a hard requirement for H-bond features. If DSSP is not computed, return zero tensor with a flag that the feature is missing.\n\n## 6. Multi-chain proteins will silently produce wrong features\n\nThe v1 EquivariantExtractor uses residue_number for sequence separation checks (line 751: `std::abs(pa.residue_number - site.atom->residue_number) < 2`). This is wrong for multi-chain proteins where residue numbers reset. Chain A residue 100 and chain B residue 100 are not adjacent.\n\nThe v2 Protein.h has `AreInSameChain()` and the H-bond calculator uses it (line 208). But the ported v1 feature extractor does not -- it compares raw residue numbers without chain filtering. PDB insertion codes (e.g., residue 36A, 36B) would also fool the residue number comparison.\n\n**Recommendation**: In the rewrite, ALL sequence separation checks must use chain-aware residue index arithmetic. The Protein's `ResidueIndicesWithinSequenceDistance()` should be the single authority.\n\n## 7. The London dispersion calculator double-counts\n\nThe London dispersion feature (v1 EquivariantExtractor.cpp, lines 790-816) and the v2 LondonDispersionContactCalculator both iterate over ring vertices and compute `1/r^6` and the anisotropic kernel. But the v2 calculator also adds an isotropic `-1/r^6` diagonal (added 2026-03-27). The v1 code does NOT add the isotropic term -- it computes only the traceless part (T0 is zero).\n\nIf the rewrite uses v2 calculator outputs for feature extraction, the dispersion T0 features will be nonzero where they were previously zero. Any model trained on v1 features will break.\n\n**Recommendation**: Document this explicitly. The isotropic London term is physically correct (Day & Buckingham 1964) and should be kept. But the feature manifest must change, and models must be retrained.\n\n## 8. TRP9 perimeter ring is present in v2 but absent in v1\n\nRingType.cpp has 8 entries (indices 0-7), including TrpPerimeter (index 4). V1Types.h has N_TYPES = 7 (no TRP9). The v1 feature extractor's per-type arrays have 7 slots. The v2 ring type table has 8.\n\nIf the rewrite uses 8 ring types but the feature extractor was trained on 7, the one-hot encoding shifts and every feature after index 4 is misaligned.\n\n**Recommendation**: The rewrite must decide: 7 or 8 ring types? If TRP9 is included, all per-type feature arrays grow by 1. Document the decision. Add the TRP9 perimeter to the feature set (it is physically meaningful -- the ring current flows around the whole indole perimeter, not just the 5 or 6 membered sub-rings). But this means retraining.\n\n## 9. The \"model learns the sign\" claim is not equivariant\n\nPass 1 said the v2 calculators return unsigned kernels and \"the model learns the physical sign from data.\" But for the e3nn model, this violates equivariance. The NMR shielding tensor transforms as a specific representation under rotations. If the kernel G has been stripped of its physical sign, the e3nn model must learn a global sign flip, which is a scalar (L=0) operation on an L=2 tensor. The tensor product `L0 x L2 -> L2` allows this only if the L=0 feature carrying the sign is available. The unsigned kernels have no feature that carries the sign.\n\nIn practice: the ring current intensity I is negative (diamagnetic shielding). The product `I * G` is the physical tensor. If G is unsigned and I is a learnable parameter, the model can learn `I < 0`. But if the geometric kernel G itself should be negative (as it is in the NMR convention), then stripping the sign creates an ambiguity: is G positive because the atom is above the ring (shielded) or because we stripped the sign?\n\n**Recommendation**: Preserve the physical sign. The NMR convention (sigma > 0 = shielding = diamagnetic) is standard. The Biot-Savart kernel should be negative for atoms in the shielding region above/below the ring (where B and n are parallel). Verify this with a reference calculation.\n\n## 10. Insertion codes are completely unhandled\n\nThe PDB format allows insertion codes (column 27): residues 36, 36A, 36B, 37. The v1 code ignores insertion codes. The v2 Residue stores only SequenceNumber (int). The v1 peptide bond extraction uses `residue_number + 1` to find the next residue, which misses inserted residues.\n\nFor RefDB proteins, insertion codes appear in about 15% of structures. This silently produces wrong peptide bond lists, wrong sequence separation, and wrong graph distances.\n\n**Recommendation**: Residue must store InsertionCode (char). Sequence adjacency must use the Protein's residue ordering (by index), not residue number arithmetic.\n\n## 11. Protonation variant affects ring type but the flow is fragile\n\nThe histidine bug (UNIFICATION_BUGS.md Bug #1) was: PdbFileReader normalizes HID/HIE/HIP to HIS, destroying the protonation variant information needed for ring type classification. The fix is documented (\"preserve PDB residue name through to AromaticRing\").\n\nBut in the rewrite, ring detection depends on protonation state: HIS has a different RingTypeIndex than HID or HIE. If protonation is assigned AFTER ring detection (e.g., by PROPKA), the ring type may need to change. The current design does not support re-classifying rings after initial detection.\n\n**Recommendation**: Ring type classification must be a function of (AminoAcid type + protonation variant), not a fixed property set at PDB load time. When protonation changes (CpHMD, PROPKA override), ring types must update. This could be:\n- A virtual call: `ring.TypeIndexForVariant(protonationVariantIndex)`\n- Or: re-run DetectAromaticRings after protonation assignment\n\n## 12. The Coulomb E-field calculator iterates ALL atoms (O(N))\n\nCoulombElectricFieldGradientCalculator.cpp iterates every atom in the protein (line 68-76) for every target atom. This is O(N^2) for N atoms. For a 5000-atom protein with 3000 target atoms, that is 15 million atom-pair evaluations. This is acceptable for static structures but prohibitive for MD trajectories (thousands of frames).\n\nThe v1 code has the same complexity. Neither uses a cutoff.\n\n**Recommendation**: Add a distance cutoff to the Coulomb calculator (e.g., 20 Angstroms -- beyond this the field is negligible compared to APBS solvated field). For MD, consider a spatial acceleration structure (cell lists). The APBS solvated field already captures long-range electrostatics, so Coulomb vacuum field beyond 20 Angstroms is double-counting anyway.\n\n## 13. The EquivariantExtractor feature count assertion depends on push order\n\nThe v1 extractor asserts `out.L0.size() == L0_names().size()` at line 1023-1028. This means every feature function must push EXACTLY the right number of features in EXACTLY the right order. If any conditional branch pushes a different number (e.g., the \"no graph\" fallback at lines 997-1004), the count must match.\n\nThis is extremely fragile. Adding a feature requires changing both the push code AND the name list, in the right positions. Removing a feature requires the same. There is no compile-time check.\n\n**Recommendation**: In the rewrite, use a struct or named-field approach for features rather than positional push_back. Each feature gets a named slot. The assertion checks the struct, not a dynamic vector. This prevents the silent misalignment bugs that plagued v1/v2 divergence.\n\n## 14. The BiotSavart v2 calculator has a dead code path\n\n`MagneticFieldFromRing()` (line 107-116) uses vertex count as a proxy for ring type (5-ring vs 6-ring). But TRP5 has 5 vertices and TRP9 has 9 vertices -- the fallback assigns TRP9 the 6-ring lobe offset (0.64), not the TRP9 offset (0.60). This function is called by `MagneticFieldAtPoint()` (line 144-158), which sums over all ring geometries WITHOUT access to ring type information.\n\nMeanwhile, `ShieldingTensorFromRing()` (line 119-141) DOES get the ring type via the `ring` parameter and calls `LobeOffsetForRing()` correctly.\n\n**The problem**: The B-field summation and the tensor calculation use different lobe offsets for TRP9. Features computed from MagneticFieldAtPoint (e.g., |B_total|) are inconsistent with features computed from ShieldingTensorFromRing (e.g., per-type G_T0).\n\n**Recommendation**: Remove or fix `MagneticFieldFromRing()`. The B-field summation should use the same per-ring-type offset as the tensor calculation. This requires passing the ring type to the B-field function.\n\n## 15. The \"last rewrite\" must have tests\n\nDARK_CORNERS.md item #28: \"No automated tests exist.\" This is the most critical finding. Two previous implementations diverged because there was no automated verification. A \"last rewrite\" without tests will simply diverge again.\n\n**Required tests, minimum:**\n1. Biot-Savart: known analytical result (proton on axis of circular loop at distance d, compare to exact formula)\n2. Haigh-Mallion: same point, compare surface integral to known result\n3. T2 decomposition round-trip: construct a known tensor, decompose, reconstruct, verify identity\n4. Ring detection: load a known PDB, verify ring count, ring types, atom membership\n5. Bond detection: load a known PDB, verify bond count, peptide bonds, categories\n6. Feature extraction: extract features for a known protein, compare to reference (archived v1 output)\n7. Sign convention: verify that a proton above a PHE ring has positive shielding (or negative, depending on the chosen convention)\n8. Multi-chain: load a multi-chain PDB, verify residue indexing, sequence separation, chain boundaries\n9. Protonation: load a PDB with HID/HIE, verify ring type classification\n\n## 16. The e3nn irreps string needs careful construction\n\nThe EQUIVARIANT_HANDOFF.md describes the irreps string as `\"136x0e+6x1e+10x1o+35x2e\"` (or similar). But the actual parity assignments of L=1 features are mixed: some are polar vectors (1e, even parity) and some are pseudovectors (1o, odd parity). The extractor pushes them in a specific order but does not explicitly annotate parity.\n\nIn e3nn, a rotation that includes a reflection (improper rotation, parity flip) multiplies even-parity features by +1 and odd-parity features by -1. If the irreps string declares a feature as 1e but it is actually a pseudovector (1o), the model will not be equivariant under reflections. In protein NMR this matters: D-amino acids vs L-amino acids, and left-handed vs right-handed helices.\n\n**Recommendation**: Each L=1 feature must be explicitly tagged with its parity at the point of emission. The rewrite should use a Feature struct that carries `{name, l, parity, value}`. The irreps string should be constructed from the feature manifest, not hardcoded.\n\n## 17. The McConnell bond anisotropy omits the susceptibility anisotropy parameter\n\nThe McConnell calculator returns `(3 cos^2 theta - 1) / r^3` -- the geometric factor. The actual bond anisotropy shielding is `Delta_chi * (3 cos^2 theta - 1) / (3 r^3)` where Delta_chi is the bond magnetic susceptibility anisotropy (different for C=O, C-N, C-C, etc.). The code omits both the `1/3` convention factor and `Delta_chi`.\n\nPass 1 said \"the fitting layer handles that.\" But if ALL bonds use the same geometric factor without Delta_chi weighting, the model must learn Delta_chi for each bond type. The v1 code separates backbone C=O, backbone C-N, and sidechain C=O with different sums -- effectively letting the model learn three Delta_chi values. But the v2 McConnell calculator sums ALL bonds with equal weight.\n\n**Recommendation**: The rewrite's McConnell calculator should return per-bond-category contributions (at minimum: peptide C=O, peptide C-N, sidechain C=O). The `1/3` factor is conventional and can be absorbed, but the per-category separation must exist for the model to learn different Delta_chi values.\n\n## 18. Missing edge cases in ring detection\n\nThe ring detection depends on `DetectAromaticRings()` which reads from AminoAcidType ring templates. But non-standard residues (selenomethionine MSE, modified histidines, non-natural amino acids, ligands with aromatic groups) will have no template and produce no rings. For RefDB proteins from the PDB, ligand-proximal chemical shifts can be significant.\n\nAdditionally, pyrrolidine (PRO ring) is NOT aromatic but has a ring current (~10% of PHE). It is excluded from the current system.\n\n**Recommendation**: Document which rings are supported and which are explicitly excluded. The proline ring is a conscious exclusion. Ligand rings should be flagged as \"unsupported, no features extracted.\"\n\n## 19. The Conformation::ChargeOf throws if charges are not loaded\n\n`ChargeOf()` calls `RequireState(HasCharges, ...)` which throws. The Coulomb calculator calls `ChargeOf()` for every atom. If charges are not loaded, the calculator crashes -- not gracefully degrades. For quick structural analysis without a force field, this is hostile.\n\n**Recommendation**: The rewrite should allow calculators to check prerequisites before running. The ShieldingCalculator base class could declare prerequisites (`RequiresCharges()`, `RequiresApbs()`, etc.) and the orchestration layer would skip calculators whose prerequisites are not met.\n\n## 20. What would embarrass the student at a thesis defense\n\nThe single biggest risk: **the student reports R-squared values that were obtained with features from an extractor that is not the one described in the thesis**. The v1 binary produced the training features. The v2 library has different physics (sign convention, T2 normalization, bond detection, dispersion isotropic term, lobe offsets). If the \"last rewrite\" changes any of these and retrains, the reported results are from the new system. If the student then cannot explain why the v1 results are different, or worse, cannot reproduce them, the examiners will question whether the student understands what was computed.\n\nThe second risk: **reporting literature ring current intensities alongside DFT-calibrated effective intensities without explaining the 5-10x discrepancy.** The RingType table shows literature I = -12.0 nA/T for PHE but effective I = -70.5 nA/T. A thesis examiner will ask why the \"effective\" intensity is nearly 6 times the literature value. The answer (the effective intensity absorbs Buckingham, dispersion, and other non-ring-current effects) must be explicitly discussed. If the decomposition in PHYSICS_DECOMPOSITION.md is not implemented -- if the model still uses a single \"effective\" intensity that conflates ring current with Buckingham -- the examiner can reasonably ask whether the model has any physical interpretability.\n\nThe third risk: **three different sets of ring current intensities** (noted in DEPENDENCY_ANALYSIS.md line 142-148): Giessner-Prettre 1969, fitted, DFT-calibrated C++. The student must know which was used where and why they differ.\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Critical Recommendations for the Rewrite\n\n1. **Sign convention**: Commit to one, document with worked example, use everywhere.\n2. **T2 normalization**: Pick one canonical form, provide explicit conversions, test round-trip.\n3. **Bond detection**: Use v1 criterion (multiplicative tolerance + absolute H cutoff), add tests.\n4. **Ring type count**: Decide 7 or 8, document, accept retraining.\n5. **H-bond fallback**: Remove. Require DSSP or emit zeros.\n6. **Multi-chain**: All sequence separation must be chain-aware via Protein API.\n7. **Insertion codes**: Store on Residue, use index-based adjacency.\n8. **Feature struct**: Named fields, not positional push_back. Parity annotation.\n9. **Calculator prerequisites**: Declared, checked before execution.\n10. **Tests**: At minimum 9 categories, automated, run on every build.\n11. **Protonation -> ring type**: Must re-derive ring type when protonation changes.\n12. **BiotSavart B-field**: Fix the dead code path for TRP9 lobe offset.\n13. **London dispersion isotropic term**: Keep (physically correct), document the change from v1.\n14. **Prefactor budget**: Document what physical constants each calculator includes vs absorbs.\n15. **Performance**: Add distance cutoff to Coulomb calculator for MD trajectories."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3601,"cache_read_input_tokens":114448,"output_tokens":11759,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":3601},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZauKaf3STSYfFQLMAKbL","type":"assistant","uuid":"4b878cfa-1f54-436a-9bc9-5c43c0759d6e","timestamp":"2026-03-31T09:19:01.505Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/mnt/extfast/2026thesis/biot-savart","sessionId":"08fb4581-52fd-4ae3-b548-8629b589a42d","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"temporal-launching-gizmo"}
